O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear son, I have completed this book which is the end of the knowledge of medicine along with its fulfillment, and have finished it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise which is part of the work of hands, namely 'surgery'.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and entirely abandoned everywhere, therefore its science has perished and been destroyed, and there remains nothing except small descriptions in books that hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and foolishness, intentions are closed off, and science is disregarded.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	But it seems to me that I wish to revive it together with the composition of this treatise according to the way of explanation and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring along the forms of cauterizing irons and other tools of the work with their arrangement and preparation as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good masters of surgery found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And therefore whoever undertakes it must climb up into the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and the number of joints, and the movement and course of veins both moving and resting, and where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And therefore Hippocrates said that "name is nothing without deed," and in the art of surgery, it is even more so.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	At the beginning of this book we told you that whoever is not acquainted with what has been said previously should guard himself lest he fall into error and kill men, just as I have often seen many people who involve themselves in this science but abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut off one aposteme of scrofula on the neck of a woman and cut the arteries of her neck; wherefore so much blood issued forth that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who drew out a stone from the bladder of a man, and the stone was large; so he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called for to remove it, and saw the condition of the sick man and the size of the stone, and knew well that if he were cut open, he would surely die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another surgeon who took in hand to cure a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the breaking there was also a wound. And the surgeon, full of ignorance, tied up the break on top of the wound with strong bandages, and did not leave any calamine for the wound, and left him thus for one term; and commanded that he should not untie it. And so it remained until the leg became completely swollen and the foot went to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come and untie the leg; and when I had undone it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the way corruption had already spread throughout the limb, and it could not be healed; and corruption did not cease to advance through the limb until the whole limb was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another surgeon who drained an inflamed black apostume and then cauterized it out of the malice of his mastery.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is purged of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all that is corrupted can be completely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you should know that surgery is divided into two parts: namely the work where there is danger in many situations, and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore you should guard yourself so that foolish surgeons cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	So take up your arms confidently, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you may come to salvation and be praised; and leave dangerous diseases to those with great skill; and put aside your arms from what causes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not undertake bad diseases lest you be called a foolish surgeon."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is of fire cauteries and of medicinal cauteries, and it is ordered from the head down to the feet; and of the forms of instruments and of the tools for cauterizing, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is of cutting and piercing, and of cupping glasses and wounds, and of extracting splinters, and similar things; and it is ordered with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is of reducing dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered from the head down to the feet, with the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, it is necessary that I tell you about the quality of each temperament and its harm.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of each temperament and its harm is the longest speech and most subtle science and secret response. And many wise men spoke about this, and agreed on it. But they allowed me few words because I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally every temperament where there is matter, except for two temperaments: namely hot temperament without matter and dry temperament without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry temperaments together with matter, some say that cautery is great help in this case, while others say the opposite: that cautery does not help against diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to treat hot illnesses with heat or dryness; and he who says the contrary claims that a cautery provides great help in treating hot and dry diseases that occur in the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	But when you compare the body and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it so by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And let no one venture to meddle therein who has not proven it and knows by long experience the art of cauteries, and the diversity of temperaments in men, and their dispositions, causes of diseases, seasons and climates; we are not afraid of other temperaments, especially cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all physicians agreed on the use of cauteries.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know this, son, that fire together with cautery is among the secrets of cures and has greater virtue than a cautery made from burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not go beyond the member that is burned, and does no harm to any other member if it could.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines spread from one member to another by scattering and cause severe inflammation in the member; sometimes they even kill the sick person.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire due to its heat and the goodness of its substance does not harm if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experience and by the length of service and study that I have devoted to the art, and was true in its entirety. And therefore I apologize for the length of my speech, for it does not please me to deprive you of the secret that is contained in fire and the quality of the work, how it expels diseases from the body, as philosophers demonstrate. Now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be made and chose priests for this purpose.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because nighttime pains are alleviated by its help. And especially when cauteries are necessary for sudden and urgent pains that cannot wait until a more serious condition arises in the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as foolish physicians do; for a disease that is healed by cautery has no recurrence. And they say so; but it is not entirely true because cauteries are not medicine that changes the temperament and dries up the humors that cause pain, and they are worth more than medicine because of their speed and effectiveness in their work and their mastery.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that a disease may come sometimes according to the temperament of the sick person and the location of the disease and its virtue. And superfluities are gathered in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things except for cauteries administered where there is little excess or moisture, such as cauteries for toothache, etc., and this pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cauteries are worth anything after medicine. Their intentions are false because when we administer remedies in any disease and they are ineffective then we apply cauteries, which are effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauteries made of gold are milder than those made of iron and they said this only because of the quality of gold and its heat. And they said that the place where a cautery is applied does not cause decay; but this is not true for I have proven it, and I found that it is true in some people. And cauteries made of gold are milder than those made of iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know exactly when it is hot because of the color of the gold and it quickly cools down. And if it is heated too much, it melts in the fire, so there are many obstacles to this method.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use iron cauteries that we have better prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have arranged this chapter from top to bottom so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two kinds made:
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a dissolving medicine moistening the head for three or four nights, according to what the virtue, age, and constitution of the patient can withstand; and then perform the cautery behind the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then make the patient sit cross-legged between your hands, with their hands on their knees; after that place the root of your palm on the root of their nose between their two eyebrows; and where your middle fingers come together, then burn and cauterize it using the cautery called "olivare", which is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	**And place him on the marked spot with ink, and do it descendingly and squeezing your hand bit by bit while twisting. Then lift your hand gently, and reward the spot if you see the bone even a little; and if you do not see it, then recommence the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; afterwards take one handful of lint, and put in soft cotton inside, and place on the spot, and leave it for three days; afterwards put on softened cotton in butter; and leave it on until the inflammation is gone; afterwards dress the wound with the ointment called 'tetrafarmaçon' until it heals.**
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	**And the elders said that when a wound remains open longer, it discharges more, and therefore this is why I assist it.**
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	"And some of these say that one should allow the cautery to burn until part of the bone is charred, and then remove what has been burnt off the bone, and it should be healed."
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	"Others say that one should place the cautery strongly enough so as to scrape off from the bone about as much as women use in their spindles, for this will allow humors to flow out; and the wound should be kept open for a long time; afterwards it must be healed and dressed."
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	"And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be good in every way, except perhaps for some people who are afraid; and I believe that one should leave it alone. For the flesh is weakened by continuous solutions from nature, as we witness in other limbs; and even when the flesh of the sick person is weak by nature, the first application of cautery seems to me to be milder and safer, and this is what I now use in practice."
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	"from the ancient pain of the head"
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	"When pain comes to the whole head and lasts for a long time, then the sick person should use herbs and pills called "cochie", and also remedies for headaches, oils, and plasters. And if one makes the cautery that we have mentioned before, it is of no avail."
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	"Be careful if the flesh of the sick person is strong by nature and not too cold; then one should apply the cautery mentioned above a little below that cautery."
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	"Afterwards, apply the cautery to each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make one cautery at the place called "vessels"; this is where cupping glasses are placed. And lift your hand so that you do not see down to the bone: the sick person feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and the cauteries on the horns must be more subtle than those used for the middle of the head, and this is how it should be done:"
dou cautere dou chief	"of the cautery of the head"
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to a part of the head, and the illness extends as far as the eye, and the head is purged by moistifying medicines, and one has made the other treatments that I have mentioned in the division of illnesses, but nothing helps: then apply cauteries in two ways, namely with medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with hot medicine is done thus: take a garlic clove and remove its skin, crush it into two parts with two kernels, then make an incision on the temple where the pain is felt in such a way that you can place the garlic clove underneath the skin; and when it has been placed, tie it firmly and leave it like that for twelve hours; then untie it and remove the garlic clove, leaving the wound open like that for two or three days; then put on cotton soaked in butter until it protrudes from the wound.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment has healed, and if you see that some burning medicines are needed, then use those that I have written about in the twelfth chapter treating burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The cautery with iron is done in this way: Heat the cautery which has this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because the head of the cautery is shaped like a closed loop with one curve, and in the middle there is a small opening. Place it on the painful spot and hold your hand steady while turning the fire slightly until half of the circle is burned; then lift your hand so that only the artery does not burn, which is located outside, allowing abundant blood to flow out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterwards, apply cotton dipped in vinegar to the wound and leave it there for three days; then put on cotton soaked in butter and continue treating the wound with ointment until it heals. If you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", which has a sharp point, be careful not to burn the artery in this migraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	de migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you are treating migraine as we have previously discussed in the divisions of illnesses, and it is not improving, and you see that neither cautery medicine nor iron cautery help, then it becomes necessary to heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it turns white. Then place it on the painful spot and make a cut about half an inch long; lift your hand once and press firmly so as not to burn the artery or reach the bone; be careful not to damage the mandible which moves when chewing, and that only the nerve is exposed without causing paralysis or spasms; also beware of excessive bleeding from the artery when it is cut, especially for those who are not used to this procedure. Leave the wound open in mid-air; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is located in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries are not helping the illness and the patient is suffering, then cauterize the wound on the head as we have discussed, and treat the wound until it heals. If you still see that there is no improvement, use the cautery described in the chapter on artery extraction with a cautery having two blades; this cautery is better and more helpful than the previous one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Here is the French text for "of the pain of the ears due to cold":
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When cold pain comes to the ear and one has opened medicinal solutions thereupon and other remedies that we have mentioned in the division, but the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "pointe"
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying the cautery all around the ear that is suffering, or around both of them if the pain is on both sides, and remove it a little ways from the root of the ear after marking the spot with an "X"; then apply ten points around each ear; afterwards treat the area until it has healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the Torture of the Mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Tortures that must be treated by cautery are only those that move from the lungs, as we have said in our division of diseases; do not apply cautery to swellings caused by congestion and spasm of the nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this swelling caused by phlegm from the lungs and nasal passages and gargarisms, and it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little way off the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make the cautery on the top of the ear a little below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as one's thumb; leave the cautery there until half of its width is burnt; this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the shape of the cautery that we have placed before you, but it is a little more subtle and the knife should be a little thicker; afterwards treat the area as I have said above until it has healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is chronic and you treat it as we have said, but there is no improvement and the patient has no fever, then apply four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the forehead, and one on the spot called "vessels" as we have mentioned before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; treat them as we have said above.
de litargie	Of litharge
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient large laxatives and pills made of mondifyings for the brain; afterwards raise the head of the patient entirely, and place on the occupit the plaster of mustard which is written about in the treatise on plasters; and that is the manner of cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healed in this way, good; but if not, apply three cauteries from the middle of the head down to the neck, and place two fingers' breadth between each cautery; treat it as you would others, and if there are any swellings, apply one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, apply two more on the two horns of the head, treating until healed. And these cauteries should be those called "olivary," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	Of coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleansed with laxatives and other remedies mentioned above. Then raise the patient's head, apply cauteries in the middle of the head, on each horn, one behind, and three on the spine of the neck; if more are needed, and the body is moist and the patient suffers greatly from a severe disease, apply four cauteries on the spine of the back, leaving them there until half of their width is burnt. Then raise your hand, treat until healed, using the cautery called "olivary" which we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The person suffering from epilepsy should not use a fire cautery unless they are phlegmatic. It is necessary to first modify the brain with remedies and other treatments that we have mentioned in the previous division, especially when the patient is large and tolerant of difficult medical treatment.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate this, perform gargling and chewing remedies that modify the brain frequently with good foods; afterwards, raise the head in the middle, and apply one cautery according to what we have said before, one on the vessel, and one on each horn; and if the patient is strong and tolerant, apply cauteries as I have said for those with paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be made of olive oil according to the method that I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, apply one subtle cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When excesses or corrupt humors are present due to melancholy, then apply the cautery of many cauteries as we have said for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the excess is inclining towards melancholy due to melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give them something to drink by which the brain may be cleansed, according to what is mentioned beforehand in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards raise the head of the patient; afterwards take a well-made linen towel, shaped like a circle, and place it on the head; and let the patient sit cross-legged, and be held securely on all sides; after that present the linen cloth, and melt mutton tallow gently over fire until the dough can tolerate it; afterwards remove the circle from inside the head and allow it to cool; and do this for the patient once a week with other good governance until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or if you wish to perform the cautery by making several punctures along the entire length of the cautery, this manner of cautery moistens the brain further; and then place on it cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the water of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When water comes first to the eyes with the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin by giving the patient something to drink that cleanses the head and guards against all moistures, and make them sweat or take several baths fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that, have the patient raise their head, and apply a cautery on the head, and apply two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of water is to both eyes together, or one cautery if the descent is to one eye; and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the heart with the cautery, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and take care not to cause bleeding of blood, and if too much blood comes out, then stop it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you how to extract the arteries and how to incise the cautery, and how you should stop it; and sometimes a cautery or branding iron is applied under the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins or near the arteries that are visible on the surface of the head, and it is seen that they are cold humid excesses, then apply the cautery as I have mentioned at the beginning of the description of water descending to the eyes: one cautery on the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or branding irons under the two rear bones; and if more is needed, then cauterize carefully above the eyebrow with several small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the division and it does not help, then give the patient three roasted pigeons to drink. After that, raise the head of the patient, and apply a cautery with olive oil in the middle of the eyebrow; and apply two cauteries called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, a little below the eyebrows; and take care not to cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the membrane of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery that is called "olivare". Here is its shape:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to do so, apply two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows themselves; and do not let your hand linger there except until about one-third of the membrane is burned, according to the manner that I have mentioned.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that points the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hair of the eyes turns inward and points at the eye, and in this case cauteries are applied in two ways: either by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the cautery by fire, command the patient to let their hair grow long and even; and if it points at its origin, pull the eyelids so that they do not move until the hair grows.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the hair has grown and is even, then have the patient lie down in your bed. Then place on the membrane of the eye a shape that is like the leaf of a myrtle plant, with the beginning of the sign near the hair; then place cotton moistened in egg white and powdered musk on the eye, then heat the cautery whose shape is as follows:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cauterize on the shape that you have marked little by little many times until the heart is burned there. The sign of the work's health is that you see the membrane retreat and the hair stand up pointing at the eye. Then lift your hand and let it be like this for three days, then place cotton moistened in butter until the burning is healed; after that, treat with ointment until it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterwards the hair comes back and the membrane is softened again, then start the cautery on that same spot as you did first. And if the hair falls out, then cauterize until the membrane rises to its natural place and is even, so that the hair does not point at the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery by burning medicine is done by commanding the patient to let their hair grow long and even. Then make a shape out of parchment like the leaf of a myrtle plant. Then take three ounces each of French soap and quicklime, grind them together well, and use it immediately so that it does not cool down. Then spread it on the shape you have made like the leaf of a myrtle plant and place it on the membrane of the eye. If the disease is in one eye only, work on one; if it is in both, work on both. Place cotton moistened in egg white under the eye. Have the patient lie down in your bed and place your two fingers on the medicine, pressing a little each time that the patient feels the bite of the medicine, for they feel the bite just as with fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, then remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when the cauterization has passed, then lift up the affected area, and observe if you see that the paper has lifted up as it would have been by constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then all is well. If not, then apply more medicine to the spot where the medicine had not opened, until your work is even and your eyes are sharp; then place cotton moistened in butter over it until the burning sensation has subsided, afterwards cleanse the affected area with ointment called 'dyafenis' and others until it is healed."
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	"And if it is necessary that you take great care in your work to ensure that no medicine falls into the eyes. And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hair stands up on end, then recommence applying the medicine onto that spot where the paper has softened properly, just as you did before; afterwards cleanse it until it is healed; this is the form of the poultice for burns."
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	"And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this you should adjust your procedures; do not follow the straight path blindly for whoever studies this art."
de la cure de fistule par cautere	The translation of "de la cure de fistule par cautere" is:
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then you must perform a cautery on it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to put their head in your hand, and hold their head between your hands so that it does not move or turn. After this, apply moist cotton with egg whites or leek juice on their eye. Then heat the cautery which is shaped like a vaulted feather, ensuring that the tip of the cautery touches the head. If you see fit, point the cautery from one end to the other, like a tent. However, the raised part of the cautery is useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After that, press the fistula if it is open and remove the pus and dry it. If it is closed, make an incision and release the bowels. Then apply the hot cautery firmly, holding your hand on the part of the cautery near the eye, ensuring that your hand does not slip. Place the cautery in the fat around the eye until corruption occurs.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you reach the bone at the beginning of the cautery, it would be good. If not, repeat the cautery once more and even a third time if necessary, then leave it for three days. After that, apply moist cotton with butter and dress the wound with a drying ointment until it is healed. If after forty days it has not healed, apply a corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed. Then treat according to what is written in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	There is another method of cauterizing a fistula which none of the ancients mentioned. Here it is:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	"And they pour one-and-a-half ounces of lead; and hold your hand firmly over the wound, ensuring that the invalid does not move or twitch, so that the molten lead does not run into his eye. It is necessary to place moistened cotton wool in front of the eye, dipped in egg whites or milk: the lead will adhere to its place and heal miraculously."
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	"If the fistula has been healed by the cauterization we have mentioned, that is good. If not, then it is necessary to administer a needle puncture and bring the fistula back into its proper place in the flesh according to what is necessary."
des crevaices en levres	"cracks in lips"
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	"Often, cracks in the lips called 'splits' occur, especially on children's lips."
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	"If you treat these cracks according to what we have said in divisions and the treatment does not work, then heat a small cautery knife according to this shape:"
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And press it quickly into these cracks until it reaches the bottom; afterwards, dress the wound with wax until it is healed."
de l’aposteme de la goule	"of the boil on the throat"
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	"When a boil comes at the root of the throat or in the tonsil, or on the palate or at the roots of the teeth, after it has become infected and rotten and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but if it does not improve: then you must have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterwards, cut or puncture the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it and on the back side; and do this once or twice, after that treat it as we have said in treatments until it is healed. And if it is cured thus, that is good. But if not, then you must uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter."
dou movement des dens	"of the movement of teeth"
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	"When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are moving, and you treat it with medicines but it does not help: then put the head of the sick person on your lap; afterwards heat the cautery whose shape will come hereafter in this manner so that you place a tube over the tooth; and put the hot cautery inside hastily, and hold your hand until the sick person feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after that, remove your hand and recommence the cautery according to your desire; afterwards, let the sick person rinse their mouth with salted water, and keep it in for an hour and then spit it out."
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	"And in this way the tooth that was moving becomes fixed, and the softened gum is strengthened, and the corrupt moisture dries up."
de la dolor des dens	"of toothache"
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	"When toothache comes from coldness, or there is coldness or wind, and treatments with medicine do not help, then it is necessary to use a cautery in two ways: a grease cautery and a fire cautery."
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	"A grease cautery is made in this way: you take wax and put it on an iron or brass spoon; afterwards, take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a needle, and dip it in boiling wax, and press it quickly onto the aching tooth and hold it until it cools; and do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth. And if you see that wetting wool and cotton in cold wax does not help, then put hot iron on it until the fire reaches the tip of the tooth."
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	"A fire cautery together is made in this way: you take an iron or brass tube that is thick enough so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the sick person; afterwards, heat the cautery whose shape will come hereafter, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools. Do this often, for the pain will be gone the same day or the next day. And it is necessary that the sick person fills their mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then spit it out. And this is the shape of the cautery:"
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	"And make a cautery on whatever head you want, according to what you have the power to do; and this is the shape of the tube:"
des scrophules	"of scrofula"
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	"When scrofula is caused by phlegm and cold moisture, and does not respond to treatments with medicine: then heat the hair cautery whose shape comes hereafter, and has two openings for the smoke to come out of the other side of the cautery; and put the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice until it reaches the base of the abscess. And if the abscess is small, use a cautery according to its size, and leave it like that for three days. And then put on moist cotton dipped in butter until the burning is gone. After that, treat the wound with ointments and dressings until it is healed."
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	"When moistures overcome the channels of the lungs, especially when this happens due to a cold complexion: then it is necessary that the sick person be first purged by solutive medicines. After that, make a cautery at the root of the throat, and make sure not to come too close to the throat, and do not burn the heart but only a little bit. Afterwards, make another cautery at the junction of the neck with the head of the spine, and use the cautery called 'clavile' whose shape we have before. And treat it like this until it is healed, as we said earlier."
de la toust	"of cough"
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all diseases of the lung are from cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or dry heat, and the disease is old, make two cauteries on the fleshy part in the places shown; and another cautery between the two breasts; and let the cautery called "clavile" be made according to the form mentioned above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor. Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:	And if you see it, make a cautery with the point that is called "poins," of which the form is shown here in the disease of the ears; and let the points be up to thirty, or as many around [as necessary]. Afterward, cure the place according to what is said above, and let there be three cauteries each on this side:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	"And because cauteries are lighter by making three at once."
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	"of the dislocation of the auxiliary ligament"
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder blade is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterward have the patient lie on their back and side; afterward lift the heart that is inside the chest with the two fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated within, then heat the cautery which has 2 inches until it reaches this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces through to the side, and there comes the figure of the cautery together with 4 cauteries; therefore the cautery is made with the cautery that has 3 inches, because the figures of cauterization are 6 cauteries; and the nerves are according to the fineness of a thread, and this is the form of the cautery that has 3 inches
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is added onto this 1 nerve, therefore there are 8 cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterward place the cautery on with a bandage of cloth; afterward let the patient rest and do not move their limbs for some time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	And if it is dislocated again afterward, which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thickness of the clavicle cautery, or many cauteries pricking. For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Regarding the cautery for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one must make for pleurisy cauteries of roots of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a root of aristolochia long and thick as you can find it, dry and also thick and also long like your two fingers; and moisten it with oil, and heat it at the fire, and cauterize 1 cautery between the armpit and the neck, and 2 small cauteries a little lower in the part that is under the beard; and 2 cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, leaning backward a little; and 1 cautery inside the breast, and another on the stomach, and 1 between the two shoulders, and 2 on the sides of the breast away from the cautery that is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand, but rather do it openly as if you were smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And some ancients said that some people used a cautery like a razor, and they heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches the aposteme; and if pain goes away, as we have said in the aposteme of the liver. But in this operation there is fear that the patient may die now, or that a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Regarding mice
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of mice according to what we have said in the division of cures, and it does not help at all, then there are 3 good ways of cautery that can be used:
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	Of these [methods], one way is such that you make three cauteries, or four, lining up according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have described earlier; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient always lie on their back.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	And another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is located at the mouse, where the rib cage of the patient comes towards the left, and let the elevation by which you lift the heart be according to the height of the body, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After this, you insert the two inflamed nerves until the heart is pierced from the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you see fit, cauterize the entire cautery with three nerves. Afterwards, when the cure has thrown off decay for a long time, this is better than the other cures mentioned earlier.
de ydropisie	Hydropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	Cautery is not effective for hydropsy, except for the manner called "ascites". When you treat it according to the methods that we have described in divisions, and your cure does not help, then you must make four cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the mouse, two behind the back on the spine, and one near the breast; and let the cauteries be well close to the chest wall.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery open for a long time to throw off decay, and do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; and healing will hasten, and both intentions will be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be like the key that we have shown before; and those for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what is depicted here.
de l’enfleure des piez	Edema of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	When the feet are swollen in a hydropsy patient and filled with yellow water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring finger; lift your hand with the cautery without turning it. And do not enter too deep, thus all the yellow water will come out, and let the cauteries be according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards make two cauteries on each leg, two on each leg at the point of the shinbone; and let one cautery be long before the knee and another behind it in the middle of the leg; leave the cauteries on for a long time without dressing until the wound closes; afterwards dress the other wounds as we have said.
de la menoison	Of the dislocation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the stomach suffers from coldness and moisture to such an extent that the retentive and digestive virtue which is in the stomach and intestines is weakened, and cannot be cured by any means of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly but with strong vitality, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said above about the cautery of the stomach, at the circumcision cautery; and four small cauteries around the mouth at intervals of one small cautery's width, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.
