And if they still do not rise up as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective against worm infection; you will find them in the section on distillations. And apply your oils and medicines to the ear with this instrument, of which the shape is shown here as you see
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or brass, narrow below with one small hole and wider above for distillation. And use a well-made brass instrument to press down inside the distillation. If you wish, take a razor and wrap cotton around its tip neatly; then pour your oil or juice into the tube, along with whatever medicines you desire. Insert the tube into the ear, then place the razor with all the cotton inside it, pressing gently until the oil has been distilled deep into the ear. Warm the distillation on the fire before distilling it into the ear, ensuring that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be effective if so.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Chapter on the Stopping of Ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with no hole in their ears; this same thing happens to adults due to injury of the ear, or flesh born inside it. Sometimes these blockages are deep within the ear so they cannot be seen; and sometimes there is one small opening missing, which can still be seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, that which comes deeply but cannot be seen is difficult to heal in many ways. However, for that which can be seen, it is necessary to put the patient's ear to the sun and look inside: if you see an obstruction appearing, then this is how one proceeds according to what is written here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And may it be sharp and cutting both before and behind, entirely full, so that it does not wound the ear; if the obstruction is flesh grown on the body of the ear, hold it with fine tweezers, and cut it lightly until all that flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the obstruction is deeply embedded in the ear, take one fine razor blade and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it on the body of the ear. If you feel the obstruction from which the patient feels pain when listening, cut lightly, taking care not to harm the nerves of the ear; then place a wick according to the width of the hole in the ear and apply Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or take a wick and moisten it in rose water, sprinkle powdered vitriol upon it, and if you see that the ear is swollen, then remove the wick and insert another one moistened in cerote made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is clean.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is discharge of blood, take a sponge and wrap it in cold water, then place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the discharge of blood which are found in treatises on distillations.
de la char des papieres	That is to say, "of the flesh of the papers"
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the remedy for those warts that come on the skin when it is moist and becomes dry, namely: extend them with tongs and tweezers, and cut them off at their roots with a spathula; then sprinkle powdered vitriol upon the wound.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if warts burst open, cauterize them with a lenticular cautery, and cauterize after the incision so that nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	Of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times there come on the skin certain things that resemble hail in shape and hardness, and therefore this disease is called "hail," and it is an assembly of thick moisture above and below the paper; the remedy is as follows: observe whether the hail moves to one side or another, which is easy to know; then make the incision wide, then scrape each part lightly, then take it with tweezers and cut it off. If you cannot cut it without piercing the skin a little, do not worry about the patient; and if the split is large, assemble it with stitches and cure it until it is healed; but if it is small, do not exert force, for ointments will soon restore it and make new flesh grow.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail descends inside the ear towards the upper part, turn back the skin and take it with tweezers and cut it off and press on both sides; and if the skin is separated by the incision, do not worry about it; and when the hail is cut off, wash the wound with salt water, and cure it with ointment that makes new flesh grow until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a grease that is produced in the threads of the skin above, and this happens more often in children than in adults, and causes great discomfort to their eyes, making them have cataracts in the mornings, so they cannot look at sunlight because tears rush into their eyes; and therefore they lie on their backs all the time and sleep on their faces, and their skin under their eyebrows is moist with the swelling and appearance covered by exinach that opens onto the eye. And when you press on the wound with your fingers, you feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the remedy is as follows: have the patient put his head in your hand; then take one linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach on each side, then place it upon him; then press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then make an incision through the moisture with a sharp spathula in the middle, not wider than the wound made when pricking for smallpox; and cut deep into the skin until you reach the exinach; and according to various conditions, exinach comes out of the wound in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take out all at once a piece of chopped meat between your fingers behind and turn your hand to right and left until it is scattered; and make sure that you do not push into the wound, so that you do not reach the whole spatula up to the eye, so as not to scratch it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the wound, then widen the wound slightly until it appears; then remove it as we have said, then moisten some linen cloths in oil and water and place them on the wound, and press with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And there are people who grind up sage and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains; then cure them until they are healed. And if a hot boil appears on the wound, then cure it with poultices soothing until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	Of the hairs of the skin
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs are born on the skin joined together other than naturally and are intertwined, they cause harm to the eyes, causing diseases such as habitual tears and softening of the skin and clouding of the eye, so that it causes blindness. And there are four ways to treat this: either by cautery with fire together, or by watery medicine according to what is said above in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by tweezers, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the patient's head in your hand, then turn back the skin of the eye with your left hand; if it is turned over, that's good; if not, stick a needle all the way through one thread above; and whether it is near the edge of the skin or where the hairs are joined together, pull one thread up to the top of the skin and turn it towards the razor; then cut into the part below the skin, below the joined hairs, with the whole spatula cutting from the large tear duct to the small one; then remove one thread, and place a small tent made of cotton and linen under the skin, then press on the skin a figure-eight shape like the mirror's fan, but nonetheless the figure must be according to the quantity that you see raising the skin that is divided by all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if one needs to cut a large amount of skin according to how much the skin is softened; then cut with the whole spatula above the two lines that you have marked, and start from the large tear duct to the small one; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put tweezers into one of the angles of the wound, then scrape it all; then bring together the two lips with a stitch of a needle with all one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and make the excess threads stick on the two eyebrows using any sticky substance if you see fit to do so; and if not, pay no mind to it, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, because the skin heals at the sewing of the wound and its joining together, but stitching is mute (as the ancients said), and this is the work without pair.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and there is another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have described, three times unfolded according to the form which is here
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut those which are above the small squares evenly according to the form which is here
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you lack the power to hold the tweezers and the thing is not even, then take a needle with one thread and put it into the figure; and put another thread beside the large ear, and the second thread beside the small one, and assemble the threads evenly between your two hands; then raise your hand evenly, and lift all the skin that you have marked, as we have described, then sew up the two lips of the wound with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if inflammation comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointment
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper is turned: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more refined.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for canines is according to this form: and it is that you turn the paper and make an incision inside according to what I have said, and then make two canines by art, and two subtle strings as long as the paper and the width of the spatula; and cut at the two places where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly onto what is above the paper of the eye, and strain the two canines from the two parts firmly; and leave it thus for a few days, and the skin that is strained will die and harden and wrinkle until it falls off by itself
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, then cut it with some force, and cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the paper has been lifted off, and the hairs will no longer point upwards; and this is the form of the two canines that you should make according to this figure and this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The operation is as follows: take a subtle needle and insert one soft and subtle silk thread into it; then tie the ends of the threads together tightly, and let the length of the threads be a palm's length; then prepare another subtle silk thread briefly and tie its end to the heads of the threads; then the patient puts his head in your hand; and stands near the sun so that the operation is clearly visible, for this is a subtle and delicate operation; then insert the needle all the way into the chase at the root of the hair next to it, and pierce the paper quickly until you pull it out through the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the chase, and insert that hair if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then pull your hand away so that the hairs come out all the way along the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the chase down along all the thread that you have prepared, until the chase comes out of the hole above and you see it through the vision of the eye; then pull the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and flesh grows over it. And if the hairs are small, accompany one long natural eyebrow hair and lift it with that one where you leave it, so that it is lengthened and then lifted up.
de la porriture de l’oil	About the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or corruption comes to the eye, there are two ways it can happen: one natural and the other unnatural. And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from an incision or cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of operating on it is that you cut open that scab and separate the lips of it, and put linen wicks inside it, and let them remain until it is healed; and do not use in its treatment things that dry out and constrict. For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before; but rather use softening things such as fenugreek; and rosewater or alum and linseed should be cooked, and ointments of diachylon melted in one of the oils, and wrap a wick around it, and treat it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you should take care that it does not heal in the same shape as before; and these operations that we have mentioned are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	About flesh growing in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is underneath is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauteries and similar things. And the manner of operating on it is that you take a needle with one doubled thread, and insert it into the flesh, and pierce it from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out at both ends of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above along the entire needle, and cut it with a broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; but if not, then take a razor and put it into the cut, and turn the paper over, and make two cuts on either side inside the paper; and let the ends of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter that has the name "gamma"; then remove that flesh according to the quantity that its sides are away from underneath, which supports the paper; then join the two separated parts together with a thread of wool; then treat it with those softening medicines and wicks that we have mentioned, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or stitches or cautery, it is necessary to cut a full incision underneath the hairs of the paper, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two lips of a wick, as I have said. And one must perform the operation according to the shape of the disease, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters devise all kinds of ways to make the figure return to its natural form. And the patient himself, according to what is necessary for the operation and instruments in various situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	About the sudden tearing of the paper (i.e., the eyelid)
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this sudden tear happens to many people in such a way that the paper above (i.e., the eyelid) is stuck with the white of the eye, and it cannot move nor perform its natural functions, then you must put the point of a razor underneath the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with tweezers, until you cut what is adhering with a subtle spatula that is not too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient can bear it and the spatula does not scratch the eye. And your incision should be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural shape. Then heal all that is assembled, and sometimes apply salt water to the eye, and rinse it with fresh water and collyrium; then put a linen wick between the paper and the eye, and put moistened wool in abduction of an egg on the eye. And after the third day, use collyrium and warm things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Thus there are two types of nail: one that is nerve-like and resembles a hard surface, and another that is not nerve-like but rather resembles congealed white moisture which cannot be grasped with tongs when touched by iron; both types begin near the large lacrimal gland and gradually cover the entire vision and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The manner of the incision is as follows: the patient places their head in your hand and opens their eyes. Then raise the paper with your left hand, use small forceps to grasp the nail from above, insert a needle into it near its base, attach one horsehair or cow hair or ox hair to it along with a strong thread, double the tip of the needle slightly and pierce it through the entire nail, tie the nail with one thread, and pull it upwards. Then scrape off the skin on either side of the nail that covers the pupil and sclera using tweezers until you reach the top, then carefully cut away any remaining tissue at the base of the lacrimal gland using a fine scalpel and small forceps, leaving the natural flesh of the lacrimal gland intact so that tears do not flow abnormally afterwards. Sometimes the nail is extended only with the onion and thread, as we have said before; then scrape it off gently with a soft spatula. This is its shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful not to touch the delicate skin with the spatula or cut it, and do not pierce the pupil. After the incision, gently apply a little crushed mallow leaves and a collyrium made from litharge to the eye, leaving it overnight. Then cure it daily until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerve-like and you cannot insert the needle or grasp it with tweezers, then this condition of nails can often be cured with medicines. As I have described in the division, if you see any growths like this, carefully scrape them away using a spoon-shaped spatula according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then carefully lift the nail upwards and if you see that it does not decrease in size and the reason remains pressed down, distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red collyrium and crushed mallow leaves, and cover the eye overnight. Then resume the operation according to this same procedure until all of it has been removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing stands in your way with the eye, such as a hot abscess, then apply the cautery, first treating the hot abscess until it is clean, then resume the work as before until it is clean.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear duct harms the eye greatly, then suspend it with a needle and cut off part but not all of it so that no tears flow into it; then apply red hot cauterization to the eye using litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Sometimes some men are born with red flesh that covers the pupil and restrains on the papillae and twists towards the outside, appearing like a mole. The procedure is for the patient to place his head in your hand, then open his eyes wide, and grasp all of this flesh with suitable forceps and support it. Then cut off this first layer of flesh, and keep cutting until you reach the end, being careful not to injure the eye during the operation. The incision should be like the one we have described for the cuticle, as shown in the diagram below:
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, then apply to the eye some crushed celandine seed or distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines onto it, and place cotton with egg white on top so that it is securely sealed against a hot abscess; and if anything remains, and hot blood overflows, and you doubt there is a hot abscess, then leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with things that calm a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is clean, and thus do for each piece of flesh joined onto the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you must align the treatment of each weak eye with its natural condition; and as for accidents, in cases involving iron, do not put your hand into any of these operations until you see that these members can tolerate this operation.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Before these veins are red and covered over the eye, they tolerate their operation and weaken the eye every day. Therefore, it is necessary that you first examine whether the eye, in which there is a sebaceous cyst, is prominent, and if there is no other external disease besides the sebaceous cyst; then treat it in this manner: Have the patient place his head on your lap, then gently squeeze these veins with all your skill, and the onion should be doubled according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And two onions per degree in a single course according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully tie those veins with force and express the blood hour after hour until you see the veins bulge out of the eye. Be sure not to cut the eye with the points of the lancets, and perform this task at midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not copiously spill those veins. And when you have done this, distill into the eye collyrium green and red to corrupt what is remaining from the sediment.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to tie everything in that hour, then make a plaster for the eye from things that calm the pain of the eyes, and leave it on for several days until the pain is alleviated and an assured hot boil has formed, then resume according to this manner that is written above until it is healed; and this is the form of the treatment:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon calls this "fistula": When you cure it by cauterization and with hot, burning medicine according to what I have said before, and yet it is not healed, then there is a trick in it that you should cut upon the boil where it must die, and remove all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness there, then take all the instruments of which this form is composed; and it is called "sharp head" and should be made of hard iron one span long, pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the level of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers and press with your hand until you know that this corruption is removed. And do this several times, then restore the level with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the level is solid and flesh grows, and the body of the brow is healed, but yet it remains like this for forty days, and it does not renew itself nor form a boil, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed. But if not, then there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form: And it is that you uncover the bone again with iron and hot medicines, and when it is uncovered then take one awl according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the shaft be tapered to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the lachrymal sac, and move your hand away from the eye a little bit, then turn the awl completely until it pierces the bone and you feel the sick person's breath through this because the wind will enter there if he holds his hand over his nose. And then restore the level with drying medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and the level hardens, then the matter goes to the nose; so it is a lighter thing for the sick person.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens completely on every side and there is no disturbance to the nose nor any narrowing, then you must bandage the sick person. Then clean him, then put cupping glasses or leeches on him without hurting him to suck, then place on the eye one linen made of aloeswood, storax, incense, and sarcocolla, and then compress the eye, and cover it with bandages and cloths. And the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and fold each one four times, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs. Then compress it with a hard bandage firmly, and recommence the cupping glasses to suck without hurting. Then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye compressed day and night, and if the linen softens, then you must change it often. Then remove the linen after the day and night, and if you see the eye improving, that's good; but if not, then recommence the compression and the cloths and the linen and the cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of a burst eyeball
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a burst occurs in the eye membrane and opens, and paper-like substances come out like a grain of resin, and it is frightening to see. Therefore if you see it happen, the procedure is as follows: You insert a needle into the root of the part below up to that above, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the lachrymal sac; And make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; Then tie off the place with the double thread and bind one part of the eye membrane tightly, then remove the needle and place damp linen moistened in egg white on the eye. And let it stay until the thread sticks with the eye membrane, then cure the eye with comforting substances until the wound is healed. And sometimes the wound is bound by the eye membrane on each side with a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has a large appearance, then pierce it with a fine spatula that comes from the bottom of the eye, and correct the white humor and let the eye descend, and enter in immediately. Then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eyelid
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This illness called "alcunnati" appears only in the eye where the bow is assembled, resembling descending water, yet it is not water; and its manner of appearance during surgery is as follows: Make the patient sit on one prepared and upright seat, then take their head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the bow rise towards your eyes. Then insert it and let it rest without lowering or shaking the light, and let the patient see things as they usually do; if it does not lower beneath, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not as we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands, then take the spatule and cut through the corneal membrane one point along the continuity of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown until the bow emerges. And when it has emerged, distill warm water mixed with honey into the eye, or water in which fennel has been boiled and honey, then treat it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Aigues of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the likeness of aigues in the division and those that it is necessary to pierce; so we work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light for the sun, and let them close the healthy eye tightly. Then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right. Then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is right. Then place the point of the instrument near the crown at the thickness of a grain in that blenchor of the eye towards the lesser lachrymal part, then gently push the instrument called "almagda" and turn your hand until it pierces into the blenchor of the eye, and feel when almagda reaches the empty space. And it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be at the depth of the measure of the space which is from the pupil up to the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the eye. Then you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the corneal tissue, and then put the instrument until it reaches where the aigue is, then express it through one way after another. If the aigue descends now, then the patient sees before them and the instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Afterward let it rest a little, and if the water rises the second way, place the wick with the instrument, and when it is well inserted and does not rise anymore, then gently withdraw almagda by turning your hand little by little. Then put again some gemmeline oil in the eye and wipe away what was inside it. Then place a plug of wool or linen soaked in rose oil and egg yolk on the outside of the eye, and tie with the healthy eye. Now, and those who are of our time, we put comminuted wormwood powder with egg yolk on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	"And then carefully pierce the conjunctiva alone, but do not go too deep; make one subtle incision, then insert the almagda as we have said. At the completion of this procedure prepare for the patient one comfortable bed where he can lie on his back in two dark rooms; let him be deprived of all movements and take light foods only; let him not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let him be bound according to his condition until the third day; then untie him in that same dark house and examine his sight; when he sees some things well, then bind him again for seven days. And know that you must not do this at the time of cautery or after incision now, but it is necessary that you alleviate this, because water rises quickly."
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	"If swelling occurs in the eye before the seventh day, then untie it beforehand and use remedies that soothe inflammation. And when it has subsided, then uncover the sight and place on his face one piece of lint to cover for a few days, and let him remain always in that dark house. Then gradually leave the house bit by bit, and turn towards his dwelling; know that no disciples should interfere with this case."
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	"And one came to us from Iray who told us that in some lands they perform cauterization with almagda, where water is sucked out, but nevertheless I never saw any of this in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing."
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	"And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda so that those who do not know them may see them; and let them be made of pure silver:"
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	"And their fronts should have this same subtlety, and their backs should have three sharp angles."
de la char sor le neis	Of flesh upon the thighs
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Among the flesh on the thighs Sometimes there appear diverse tumors of which some seem like scorptions with many legs and others have flesh colored purple or soft flesh colored white. In that soft flesh however not purple, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils and sprinkle powder on those tumors; then scrape off what you can hold with a sharp scalpel until you know that all the flesh has been removed
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any that cannot be scraped off, open it with one of the sharp instruments lightly so that nothing remains; and if it swells or becomes inflamed, treat it as needed; and if they are malignant ulcers, hurry to cauterize them until the blood is stopped and all the flesh removed, then sprinkle on the thighs powdered resin or wine
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the tumor opens and moisture comes as far as the palate, know that it is harmless; but if moisture does not flow as needed, know that there is new flesh growing into the bone above, do not use the instrument to cut: therefore you must insert one thread of thick linen moistened with hot water and seasoned with a half or less of a doit of incense on each end; and let the patient hold the thread in their tumor with moderate force and draw it out smelling until it comes through the nose into the mouth; children at school often do this, and it is easy for whoever wishes to do it; then hold the head that comes out of the nose with one hand and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand and know which end is in front by feeling it. Do this until you know that the ends have rotted all the flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe off the blood, moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment and put it back into the tumor as before; do this for three days or more until the ointment has eaten away all the remaining flesh, then put a plaster of lead on it for some days until it is healed, and if there is need of drying medicines use them; and this is the form of the instrument used to purge the head, from which oils and medicines are distilled
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is made of silver or brass resembling an open lamp like a tube with its conduit also; and if you wish, make a closed tube and fill the instrument to purge the head, having many holes at the top for holding it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	To remove flesh from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises on the nose a disease called "telul" which grows and becomes large enough to be seen plainly; for this reason you must cut it off at the beginning and remove all of its base, then put on it cautery or burning medicine. But if it is delayed until it becomes large, take care if it is hard, of foul color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron for it is an enchanted aposteme, because when it is cut some great harm comes to the sick person; but if the aposteme is soft to the touch, not of foul color, and you see that it can all be cut off, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure it afterward with drying and constraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and bleeding
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when inflammation occurs in one of these cartilages,
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is thus: you bring together the edges either by needles, as we have said in abdominal suturing; or by thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	lipomas
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men develop hard tumors inside the lips, resembling grains of wheat in size and shape, some small and others large. Therefore, you should turn back the lips and cut into each one with a knife, grasping them with forceps and cutting into each part. Then fill the space after incision with powdered vitriol until the blood stops flowing, then apply a bandage and cure the area with dry substances until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of gum tissue
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often on the gums there grows adherent flesh called "albulus" by the ancients; one should grasp it with forceps and cut it at its root, allowing the blood vessel or vein to run freely. Then apply powdered vitriol or other restrictive and drying powders to the area. If this flesh returns after incision, which often happens, then cut it a second time and cauterize it. After cauterization, it will not return. This is how one uses instruments to cut.
des sordens	of boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes warts appear at the head of teeth inside the mouth between the gums, which are unsightly and rough. Sometimes teeth become black, greenish yellow, or wormy, such that decay reaches the gum tissue, causing a foul odor. Therefore, make the sick person sit between your hands with their chin in your lap, and scrape away all the warts until nothing remains. Do likewise for blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains until they are removed. If you remove what caused them at first, it is good. If not, then resume scraping on the second and third day until everything has been scraped away. Know that teeth require various tools to scrape according to what the task demands, for those used to scrape off excess tooth material have different shapes than those used to scrape between teeth. Have these shapes and others readily available.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary, when you treat a toothache, to delay pulling it as long as possible, for this should not be done; for it is a substance very high until one has no excuse for drawing [it].
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained to have a tooth pulled, it is necessary that you be certain about the aching tooth. Often times the pain leaves the patient, and they think it is in a sound tooth, and have the good tooth pulled; but still the pain does not depart at all because of the evil extraction we have already seen done by these surgeons. And when you are well certain about the aching tooth, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth with a sharp instrument strongly to guard the gum on all sides; then move it with your two fingers or with fine forceps bit by bit until it is well loosened, then firmly hold the forceps. And let the patient's head be in your lap between your knees, and keep yours still so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	"Next, extract the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then use one of these instruments and place it gently on each side, and move it as you have done before. And if the tooth is perforated and rotting, then you must fill the hole with wadding where the perforation is; and grasp it subtly with pliers so that it does not break while extracting it; and there must be much bleeding around the gum to loosen the tooth."
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	"And make sure you do not break it, and if some part remains, the patient may experience greater pain due to the wickedness of the root. And beware that you do not act like the ignorant surgeons who, because of their haste and boldness, sometimes break the jawbone and do not accomplish what we have described; but often bring on great illnesses through the negligence of those roots that remain there, or through the jawbone that they break, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with wine or sage and salt water. And if blood flows from it, which often happens, then fill the place with powdered vitriol; and if this does not help, cauterize it."
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	"The shapes of the instruments with which one first moves the teeth should be long and thick at the handles, so that they do not double over when you pull the tooth; and these are their shapes:"
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	"And they should be of thick members so that they do not bend during extraction, and they should be made of good iron and have teeth to hold the tooth in place."
de la racine des dens	"for the root of the teeth"
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	"When the root remains after extraction, you should place on the wound cotton moistened in butter for one or two days until the wound is softened. Then insert into it the pliers called 'algefri', which resembles a crow's beak internally and is made like a rasp. And this is its shape:"
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if the roots will not come out with all these pliers, you should uncover the flesh entirely around the root and insert into it the instrument called 'althali', which is like a spatula. And this is its shape:"
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	"And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break. And if the root comes out through this, that is good. If not, help yourself with all the instruments, of which the shapes come hereafter:"
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	"And also help yourself with this instrument which has two rows, of which this is the shape:"
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	"and other iron instruments that are placed in front of the root of the teeth, and also help yourself with this instrument which resembles large pliers. And here is its shape:"
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	"And this instrument should be strong so that it cannot break. And know that there are many instruments for teeth; and also others that are not counted here. And the wise and subtle master finds his own instrument according to what his works and the illness show him, because there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity. But if you break something of the jawbone or other bones, then search for the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and help yourself with gestures. And here is its shape:"
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	"And they should be thick and hold well to grasp the bone without slipping, but so that it can hold and remove it. Then restore the place with suitable medications according to what is needed. And if there is decay in the bone, even if it is small, then remove it with all these instruments."
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	"When the tooth appears not according to its natural course and is misshapen, especially in young women, you should know if the tooth is next to the tooth and not in its right place, so that it cannot be set or smoothed: then scrape it off. And if it is attached to the tooth, take this instrument of which here is its shape, resembling a small beak, and made of good iron pointed at the end:"
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	"And work little by little with your hands over several days to remove the tooth because of its hardness and so that you do not move the others. And if it is visible enough to be smoothed, then smooth it with a rasp like this one here, of which this is its shape:"
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	"And it is also like the rasp used to make needles. And smooth the tooth little by little each day lightly so that it does not fall out too soon. Then polish it at the end with any sharpener. And if the tooth is too pointed and wounds the tongue, then smooth its sharpness until it is even so that it neither wounds the tongue nor disturbs speech."
