quant li dent lochent	"When teeth are loose:"
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	"When front teeth are loose, either from trauma or a fall, and the patient cannot chew their food without them falling out, even after treating them with tightening medications, if they do not work: then you must tighten them with a gold wire because silver wire turns green and decays. And the wire should be neither too thick nor too thin according to the space between the teeth. If you see that the teeth are crooked, take the wire and bend it double between two healthy teeth, then place the loop around the loose tooth or teeth until you reach a healthy tooth on the other side. Then start wrapping again from the beginning up to where you started, pulling your hand tightly but carefully so that the teeth do not move. The tie should be tight at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut off the excess wire with pliers and attach it between the healthy tooth without hurting the tongue. Leave it as tight as possible until it can remain in place, and if it comes loose or the wire breaks, then tighten it again with another wire. And this is how they should remain throughout their lifetime. Here is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of two healthy teeth and two loose ones:"
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	"And when a tooth falls out, it should be replaced in its place little by little as we have said. And only wise and skilled people should intervene, and sometimes the shape of a cow's bone tooth is made and placed where the tooth is missing, then attached just like we described earlier. And this serves for a long time."
de coper lou liien de la lengue	"To cut the tie of the tongue:"
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	"Sometimes there is this tie that comes from underneath the tongue or is born naturally; or due to an injury caused by a wound. And here's how you perform it: open the patient's mouth and have their head resting on your lap, then raise the tongue. Then cut the nerve tie as far as possible without cutting too deeply so as not to damage the artery underneath. If there is any scarring or new tissue growth due to the injury, use a forceps and cut the tie from above. After you've finished, apply rose water and sage compresses or cold water compresses, then place a linen bandage under the tongue each night to prevent healing. If bleeding occurs, apply powdered vitriol on the wound. If bleeding persists, cauterize it with a lentigo cautery, which is very good for this purpose. Then treat it further until it heals completely."
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	"and if you see it is of dark or black color or hard so that the patient does not feel it then do not touch it for it is cancer; and if it tends towards blenching and there is moisture there then throw on it ointment, and open it with a sharp scalpel, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if blood flows at your operation then put powdered vitriol until it stops flowing, then return to your operation until you draw out all the pus; then raise the area cleanly and carefully, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed."
des apostemes de la gorge	"throat abscesses"
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	"Godath", also called the two mandibles, sometimes occur in the throat. If they are not cured as mentioned earlier and appear as hard, narrow boils with a dark color, do not touch them with iron.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue against this instrument and see the boil, use tweezers to pierce it and twist it upwards as much as possible. Then wipe some cloth with it before using the instrument to squeeze it out, which resembles a pair of forceps. The tips are curved towards each other and very sharp, made either from iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	"And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then take pincers, of which here is the form:"
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	"And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have gripped one of the almonds, then grip the other in the same manner, and afterwards gargle the patient with warm water mixed with salt or rue, and if there is bleeding, gargle the patient with water or cooked pomegranate skins, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stanched; then continue treatment until it is healed. And sometimes other abscesses than these two almonds develop in the throat, so grip them in the same manner as the two almonds."
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	"And I treated a woman for an abscess that had grown inside her throat, namely one small abscess; and she could barely breathe at all because the passage was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died within one or two days if left like that. The abscess had grown so large that it had filled two fingers' length. I therefore acted quickly, and inserted a needle into one of the openings, then drew out a large portion of pus; then I reinserted the needle into the other opening in her throat, opened her mouth and pressed down on her tongue; afterwards I inserted the needle into this abscess and cut off part of it, from which only a little blood came out. And thus the passage to the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began drinking water and then wine, but for a long time I kept cutting away at this abscess as it grew back again and filled in the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I cauterized it with a hot iron inside her throat: thus it ceased to grow. And I left these parts, and do not know what God did with her afterwards."
de l’uve	"de l’uve"
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When it comes down to the eye, and it is inflamed and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, thick and rounded, it is called "eye". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help at all, and you see that the hard abscess is quieted, but it is subtle, then it must be cut; and that which is rounded together and is not elongated. And it is sanguineous or brown colored or black, then you should avoid cutting into it. For there is great danger to the patient in doing so. Therefore, when you see it according to its appearance and length, make the patient sit before the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the onion into the eye, and draw it down, and cut with one or two instruments that we mentioned in the incision of the two almonds. And do not cut more than the natural limit, for if you cut more, you will injure the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and continue the cure until it is healthy. And if the patient fears being cut, then you should use a device for cauterizing with fear. The manner of cautery is thus: let the patient put their head on your lap, and then press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and confect with boiling water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and this is its shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	**And let there be at the top a vessel into which one puts the medicine, like the horsemen of a spoonful, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and the patient should lie on their side so that saliva and mucus run from their mouth to the medicine within, so that it does not descend to the throat or the bladder. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it upon the eye for the quantity of half an hour until you see it is blackened and the marks of the medicine have ceased; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with all the cotton in the vein above until the cotton touches the eye; and do this often until the cauterization is complete. Then let it dry and fall after four or five days. And if you need to recommence the cautery of the medicine, then recommence it, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse that which is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured with gargarisms until they are healed.**
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	**This cure is safer than incision or cauterization; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and mugwort and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them into one pot, and put it on the fire to boil. And let the pots be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot there should be an instrument shaped thus:**
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	**And let it be of silver or brass, and one of the ends of the instrument should be placed in the mouth of the sick person so that the vapor rises to the eye through the vein until the eye is mortified. Then recommence this often until the eye dries, and guard yourself so that you do not perform this at the beginning of the coming of a hot aposteme, for many things happen there; and do not perform it before the decline of a hot aposteme. And if this instrument is not present, then take a vein and put inside its end an eggshell, so that the mouth of the sick person does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not let the vapor harm the mouth, and this is a good cure together.**
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	**Many times there is a bone or fish spine stuck in the throat, or some other thing; therefore you must draw out that which you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument so that you see it move. And that which does not appear to you and is hidden in the throat, it is necessary for you to make the sick person vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps by vomiting the thing will come out. Or the sick person should swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of flannel, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will catch on, and then draw it out. And if it does not come out from what we have said, then take an instrument of lead in this shape:**
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	**And let the instrument be bent at its end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the end raised high. And guard yourself so that you do not touch the epiglottis, but take care that all of it is gone, nor should you push the bone inside; and it is better for the sick person to put in the instrument themselves, so that they know where the thing is stuck; then draw it out evenly along the whole length of the instrument until it comes out.**
de la sansue de la gorge	**de la sansue de la gorge**
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No translation provided for the first line: "Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue..."
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with assfetide, using the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye. Do this many times, for it will fall without hurting. And the manner of fumigation is that you take one pot which has live coals, and let the bottom be covered with a pierced cloth in the middle, and in that hole put the end of the instrument; then throw your fumigation into it, and the patient puts the head of the pipe in his mouth and closes the mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes as far as the tonsil; and the tonsil will fall now, and if it does not fall, then begin the fumigation again many times. And let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and alkaline things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	"And the shape of the instrument with which one treats a vein is thus: when it can be seen, it resembles bent forceps for entering into the throat; and it has the appearance of a crow's beak, and has the sharpness of a file so that what it grasps, it cannot let go."
li chapistres des apostemes	"Chapter on Abscesses"
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what is written here from one and another in this book, and they are divided into perforation and incision; and there are two ways about this, one in its own likeness, and those that it holds moist. And the second way is for the places where they are on the body, because the abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and the abscesses of fleshy parts are different from those that come into joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	"And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the bowel has completed its natural course; and there are those which must be pierced when they have hardened, and do not die according to their natural course, like abscesses near joints. For when an abscess appears near a joint, if it is left alone until it becomes completely hard, then perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint may become damaged, causing contraction in that limb. Or the abscess may be near the main limb, and if you delay piercing it until it is too late, it will harm the main limb; or if it is near the fundament, it should be pierced before it dies. One must not pierce a hardened abscess without having completed digestion, except for one that is near the fundament which might otherwise penetrate deeply and become adherent, forming a fistula which cannot heal in a short time."
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	"And you must know the time for piercing an abscess that has completed its natural course, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the fever subsides, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs. And you must perform the incision where the abscess hangs down the most, and where it appears to be dead; and the incision should be long according to the length of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints near nerves and arteries, and in all smooth places where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	"And in those that are folded, according to the shape of that member. And when an abscess is in fatty tissue, it is better to wait for the incision until it has completed its digestion and is well formed, as we have said before. Because if you pierce it beforehand, then the body of the venom will be spread out, and it will be full of much filth; and perhaps the edges and depth of it may become hardened. And there are some abscesses that should be pierced according to the width of the body, depending on what the member needs. And you must make small incisions for small abscesses, small holes; and for large abscesses, large holes, and many slits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess. And there are some abscesses where one must cut out the core and cover it, when they have become like a penny in size, and are softened, then one should do as with boils: And there are those that are slit into three angles, and there are those which are cut like a fig leaf, such as armpit abscesses; and there are those where one makes a round cut, and other cuts of similar shape."
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Those that have no head, such as soft superficial abscesses, should be pierced plainly. And when the abscess is large and has swollen greatly, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at once, but draw out a part of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more again; do this many times gradually until all the pus comes out, especially if the patient is weak, or pregnant woman, or small child, or elderly man. Because sometimes the spirit jumps with the exit of the pus, and perhaps the patient may die, and you would not know it. Therefore be careful in this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, examine the wound to see if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a plain incision, then apply linen or old cotton pads; and if it is a large abscess with many holes, then you must stuff each one with a pad so that they come together. And if you have cut off a piece of skin in the abscess and have removed it around, then you must fill it with dry cotton or linen cloth lint without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it, and apply ointment until it is healed."
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if bleeding occurs from your operation, then bring cold water and a little salt, and moisten one cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times. And if the bleeding persists, then apply dressing and care, and the powders that I have said in my hands in this book, in their appropriate places. And if it is in winter time, and the place where the abscess is very nervous, then you must put wet cloths and warm wool pads on it; and if it is in summer, and the place is fatty, then you must put wet cloths in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, for three days, as we have said before; then untie the abscess and wipe it clean, and apply the appropriate treatment until it heals."
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	"And this is what one must know universally in the cure of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the cure of abscesses, and here is the chapter."
des soros	chapter on boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	"Know this about boils on the head: small abscesses come from them, which are like those in wool, similar to a hen's nest, and there are many such cases. Some are fatty and some contain moisture like pimples; and there are also hard and stony ones at the incision, and there is no doubt that an artery opposes it. The operation for the incision is this: you squeeze with an instrument called 'entromissoire', which comes from a form given below, to see what it contains. For if it contains moisture, then cut open over its length. And when the moisture has been drained out, then scrape off all the skin that contained that moisture, for it will always return if you leave anything behind; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if available; if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound with it and leave it until the next day; then repeat this process of cotton on the second and third days until you know well that there is no more moisture left; then apply appropriate ointment to heal it until it is healthy. And if the boil contains a lot of fat, cut it open along its length; scrape out your threads, and scrape off all around, and focus your treatment on pulling out the coat where it lies; and if an artery opposes you, do what I have said after this."
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	"And cutting into the abscess that is pierced and moist is easier, for they are lacking in blood. And there are some of these abscesses at the head where there is no moisture, like those .i. abscesses that I copied at the head of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if one had struck any, it would have made just as much wound as from a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, except those which come to the heads of children and at the roots of ears, let the incision always be at the lowest dependent point, so that the bowels may exit more easily; and cure them as is proper."
des scrophules	"Regarding scrofula"
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the buttocks, and in angles, and sometimes they come to other parts of the body, and there are many of them, and they are interconnected. And each scrofula is properly inside its own bone, like the knot and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similar kinds of these scrofulas. Some contain moisture, and some are malignant which do not wish to obey health. Therefore, when you see one that is well-disposed to touch, and is like the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not hard against the nerves of the neck nor the artery nor the vein, and is not deep; then you should cut it from above, and scrape from each side, and press the two lips of the heart together once if you need to, as we have said for head abscesses; and cut little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and let not the scalpel be too wide nor cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and do not cut too deep, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and it does not allow you to work, then put powdered vitriol or some powders that stop blood in the wound, and constrain the wound; and let it stay until the abscess is appeased, and the wound begins to soften and start to rot. And when the blood is staunched, then return to your work until you finish it; then seek with your index finger if there remain any small scrofulas, cut them out and cleanse them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, then it is not necessary for you to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall without harm; then fill the wound with thick cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them up immediately, so that there is no excess flesh left due to the size of the scrofula. Then you must carefully cut the root of it and draw out any pus, and sew it up as we have said. Those scrofulas that contain excess flesh should be pierced where they appear largest; pierce them in this way: first make a small opening with a scalpel, then dilate it little by little until you reach inside the scrofula. Then bring together the edges of the wound and sew them up immediately, so that there is no excess flesh left. Then apply dressings with ointment and similar things to cause what remains of the corruption to rot. And when the wound is well cleansed, then cure it with ointment on fresh flesh until it is healthy.
de squinance	Here is a possible translation of "de squinance" into English:
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of cutting the throat;
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	In those who have swelling,
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat of the lung, it is necessary to close the epiglottis to escape the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to split the epiglottis, it should be done below three or four circles with a small cut across, between two circles or according to the amount of the slit in the soft palate, but not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those places are connected to the epiglottis cut such that there is no flesh there, and the vessels are long and thin.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is afraid, he should stretch the skin of the throat all along the incision, then cut into the heart until it reaches the channel; avoid the blood vessels if you see any, and then close the soft palate as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And this is demonstrated by the section of the larynx channel that jumps out through the spot that is broken, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leaves the wound open for a while
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour of doubt about strangulation has passed, join together the two lips of the wound in the heart and sew it up smoothly without the cartilage; then administer medications that promote healing until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be near death, and the breath is gone.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, cut off the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, thus being saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	"And for this reason, the ancients commanded that one should leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four."
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	"And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and treat it until it was healed."
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	"I will tell you what I saw."
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	"I saw that a damsel took one knife and stabbed it into her throat and cut some of the vessels of the lung."
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	"and I was called to heal her, and found her as dead as could be."
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	"I uncovered the wound and found that the blood issuing from it had not cut any vein nor carried off the throat, but the windpipe issued forth through the wound."
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	"I rushed to stitch up the wound and treated her until she was healed;"
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	"and nothing happened to the damsel except that she became hoarse of voice, and afterward returned to her former condition."
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	"Therefore I say that in the operation on the epiglottis there should be no fear."
de la grosse gorge	"of the large throat"
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	"This hernia is called 'throat hernia', and it is a large bubble of purple color that occurs mostly in women;"
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	"and there are two kinds of it: natural and acquired; or the latter has no engine."
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	"And there are two kinds of accident: one is similar to fatty tissue, and the other is similar to an arterial hematoma."
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	"And there should be fear in this case, and one should not operate except on the small ones, and the proof and search should be made throughout the introitus."
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	"If you find it like a fatty tissue and not attached to any vein, cut it as you would cut a fatty tumor, and excise it completely if possible;"
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	"and search carefully all around it, and treat it as necessary until it is perfectly healed."
des nous	"of fatty tumors"
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	"There are many kinds of fatty tumors, each with its own appearance, which I will describe;"
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	"And now it is necessary for me to explain the entire difference between a fatty tumor and an hernia."
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	"I say that an inflammation and fever accompany it until the ebullition has passed, and then corruption is completed; afterward the fever and heat subside."
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	"With a fatty tumor there is no heat or fever nor pain, and it contains fat, which is its own sac and is the same color as flesh, beginning like a bubble and becoming large;"
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	"and there are two kinds of them, either fatty or moist, and most of them are the same color as I have described in the classification."
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	"When you come to the treatment of fatty tumors, first examine and explore with the instrument called the 'introitus', according to its form as described in the chapter that follows."
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	"The manner of examining fatty tumors is to take the moistest part that you find in the tumor and twist it gently bit by bit until you know that the instrument has pierced the heart of it, according to its size;"
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	"then remove the introitus, taking care not to let anything leak out."
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	"If moist corrosive humor is flowing from it, whatever its color may be, cut it as I have described for other tumors;"
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	"and if no moist humor comes after the introitus, know that it is fatty and cut it in a cross shape, grasp it with forceps, and lightly scrape away the skin on each side and the coat in which it lies, so that you may draw it out whole with the tumor."
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	"And if you cannot draw it out whole, remove it piece by piece until nothing remains."
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	"For if anything remains, the fatty tumor will return many times;"
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	"and if a bit remains and the skin troubles you, sprinkle some caustic waters on the wound, bandage it tightly, apply soothing poultices for tumors with heat, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed."
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	"And if the fatty tumor is large, cut the two lips of the wound and treat it like a wound that involves flesh."
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	"And if a pulsating vein opposes you or another obstacle, hurry and apply powdered vitriol to the place, leaving it on for two or three days until the wound has corrupted and the ebullition of blood has subsided; then return to cut what remains of the fatty tumor."
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	"Here are the shapes of the introitus instruments, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are four squares called 'albaret', and one called 'breb', and there are also three kinds to encircle fistulous tumors;"
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	"and they are like the needles used to cut out warts, made of brass or iron or silver, with those of yellow brass being most valued, and they are best suited for encircling the curves of fistulous tumors;"
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	"and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings."
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	"The shapes of hooks are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are hooks with two curves that come in three kinds;"
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	"And there are hooks with three curves that also come in three kinds; and there are hooks with two curves and hooks with one curve only, which are also of three kinds; all of these are necessary for their respective uses."
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	"The tips of these hooks are cutting, and there are some that do not cut but only scrape off fatty tumors so as not to injure veins or nerves;"
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	"And among these introitus instruments are the almond-shaped ones that fit into hands so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of tumors;"
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	"and they come in three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see;"
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	"And these are only used where the flesh is thick, such as in thighs, arms, breasts, and angles, and similar places;"
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	"And sometimes another small instrument resembling the scrapers for fistulas is made according to this form, with which blood is wiped away:"
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	"and it is placed sometimes at the location where veins and arteries have been cut, and sometimes they are made according to this large form:"
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	"Sometimes the breasts of some men swell up when they begin to be corrupted until they seem like women's breasts;"
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	"And they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them must do so according to this form from line B to G:"
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	"then scrape away the fat, apply a medicinal poultice for wounds involving flesh, then join together the two lips of the wound to stitch them up, and treat it until it is healed;"
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	"And if the breast hangs down and is enlarged like that of a woman, then it is cut in two places above along two similar slits;"
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	"So that one is attached to the other at the end of each, so that the larger part contains the smaller according to this form from line B to G;"
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape off the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed, or the incision is not complete because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it until it consumes the remainder and the fat, then heal it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	swellings of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These hard swellings that appear under the arms are types of scrofulous tumors with hard edges, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture must be cut along this line from point b to point g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the boil is emptied out, then fill the wound with old cotton and leave it overnight, then remove all the cotton and heal it with suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the swelling resembles scrofula, cut it as we have said in the section on scrofulous sores, and if the wound secretes pus, apply a cautery as we have said earlier.
de la routure de l’artere	of the bursting of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery bursts and the skin above it is adherent, many swellings often result, and the same happens with a varicose vein and swelling.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows that it is due to an artery, then the swelling will be long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	"When you feel it with your two hands, then sense one pulling; and when it's due to the vein, then there is an evident deficiency."
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	"It is foolish to attempt to conceal this tumor, especially when it occurs under the armpits and around the ankles or neck, and many other places; and it can become quite large."
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	"Therefore, the treatment with iron should be avoided, and also for the one at the head, and in the case of swelling from an artery cut through the skin."
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	"Then tie around the wound like a tourniquet and neatly separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed."
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	"Then place a needle underneath one side and pierce it through to the other side, tying the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have shown you before regarding the extraction of the two arteries in the temples."
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	"Then insert a probe between the two ties at one spot until blood comes out and the tumor is released."
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	"Then apply the treatment with all due care until the bandages fall away."
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	"Then treat it with an appropriate ointment until it heals without complications."
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	"And if the tumor is due to the tension of the vein, then you should cut around it with your hand from the tumor throughout the skin,"
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	"Then place the needle underneath the spot you are holding with your hand and pierce it through, leaving one doubled thread on that side so you can pull it out from the other side."
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	"Then tie off the tumor as I have told you, using one of two ties made with thread at both ends."
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	"And if you doubt that the thread will not slip out, then insert another needle through both threads underneath the entire tumor along the incision of the first needle and tie the threads at four places."
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	"Then cut off the tumor until excess fluid comes out, then cut off the excess skin and leave what is tied."
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then place a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply compresses and dressings until it heals."
des apostemes des ners	"Apostumes of the nerves"
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, boils come to the artery and vein,
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	"Dislocation happens more frequently in the shoulder and hip joints, and in all places where there are joints; this is one serious abscess, with a color resembling that of the body, but often without pain."
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	When it [the dislocation] is pressed strongly, the patient feels pain; however, this pain is not deep within the body, but rather below the heart.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	"And moves well on all sides,
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	"And one who is on the head or forehead, makes the skin tender at the temple."
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	"If the abscess is small, you should grasp it with tweezers and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if it is large, suspend it with a towel and scrape it off, then clean the wound and sew it shut, treating it until it heals."
des grosses boces pendans	"from hanging bags of fat"
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	"Sometimes happens in bellies and nowhere else but there, and it is called 'fungus' by its appearance, with roots being fine and excrements large, some small and others very big."
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	"I saw one man who had two on his belly that resembled mushrooms more than anything else, with no difference, being white and having small roots and cracked open with moisture constantly flowing."
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	"I weighed them and found one weighing eighteen ounces and the other six pounds; the wound opened by cutting into it shows whether the patient is moist, with the flesh being pale, moist, and having fine roots."
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	"If the cut is large, have cautery irons ready nearby, because there often comes too much bleeding at once, and if blood flows too quickly, hasten to apply the cautery."
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	"And if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision from iron, then take one well-made thread of linen, tie the flesh as we have described, and leave it for two days."
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	"And then tighten it, and do not cease pulling the linen thread until it cuts through the flesh, and let excrement pass through without effort. And if the roots are large, fear cutting them altogether because of the belly, but you can still cut half of them."
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	"Then cauterize to prevent it from coming back; then dress the wound, and make sure not to cut the teat which is fox-colored, has poor sensation, and produces milk."
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	"For this is an enchanted aposteme, and I will speak of the cure of chancre later on."
quant li boude ist fuer	"When the belly is full"
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from a cautery burn or a slit in the skin's surface, and is located on the belly or in one of its folds, as happens in other wounds, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries, according to what is stated above, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is due to an injury of the skin and the eruption of a boil, then the color of the aposteme resembles the color of the body, and there is little pain or discomfort, with various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to an intestinal issue, then it becomes more diverse, and when pressed with two fingers it sinks in and then returns, and sometimes it becomes hard, and increases greatly at the entrance of the bath and with heavy labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is light and opens well when pressed with the hand, causing no constriction. But if it is due to blood, then the boil appears large and hard, with these signs: it feels fixed according to its size;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to windiness, then it feels soft to the touch. The opening will show whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery or vein, or simply windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Therefore you should leave it alone. For there is doubt and fear concerning it, as I have told you in the chapter on boils, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the bowel, then you should command the patient to tie their bellyband and lie down straight, then press all around the boil;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	Then have them lie on their side between your hands
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place you have marked with the whole spatula
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then stretch half of the boil upwards with the entire large forceps;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then tie it around tightly with a strong thread or silk cord, and let the knot be well tied
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open half of the boil stretched out above the tie, and insert your index finger inside to find the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught in the tie, then untie it, and bring the intestine out through the opening in the belly
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the bowel, take it with the forceps and cut off any excess
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery or vein becomes visible to you, then carefully go around it, and then return to your work and take two needles, and attach two strong threads to them, and insert the two needles in a cross pattern where you have pierced;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then press the boil in four places above the needles, and if you see blood, remove the needles, leave the opening until it stops bleeding, and cut away any dead flesh.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	Or you can cut it when it is subtle and porous, then treat it as needed, and cut the boil as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And remove the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the opening as necessary, and stitch it up.
dou chancre	chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of cancer the similarities of cancer, and how one should operate with medicines, and how to avoid surgical treatment. And we say that cancer that affects the marrow is dangerous, and requires great caution in treating it. The ancients said that when cancers are located in places where they can be scraped away like cancers on the breast or hip, and similar locations, they must be removed entirely at the beginning; but when they are large and old, one should not approach them, for I have never seen anyone cured of them, nor has anyone been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once, then make them vomit if they show signs ofpletion, then prepare the patient well for the operation; then cut off your forceps and cut around the cancer completely and remove it completely without leaving anything behind; let the blood flow freely and press the wound tightly with your hand or something else, and if bleeding from the incision of the artery or vein becomes troublesome to you, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the collection of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the treatment that is done with medicines, and that which is done with iron: only "eclites" is mentioned here; and one should not touch it with iron in these two similarities: namely tympanites and yposarche, for they are deadly things. Therefore, when you treat this dropsy similarity called "eclites" with medicines and the treatment does not help, look to see if the patient is weak or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as inflammation of the bowels and similar things; do not touch it with iron for there is doubt about it. But if you see that the patient has strong vitality, and they have no other illness but dropsy alone, and they are not too young nor too old, then you should operate thus:
