Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many types of boils occur in the anus, such as chancre and pus-filled boils, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot boils, as well as other diseases that I have mentioned previously. Therefore, I must discuss in this treatise the hot boil that occurs in the anus, which is not one of those boils that form on the buttocks; if you wish to know how to treat it, look at whether the boil is hard and inflamed at the beginning of its appearance, full of heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it. Do not rush to pierce it, but make it suppurate until the pain subsides; then have the patient sit on one seat with two small seats where they can recline, leaning their back against them and placing their feet toward the hips; spread their thighs apart, place their arms under their knees, and tie them securely with a good bandage; then suck out the pus from the right side, prepare the instrument used to open the anus, of which I will give the form below; it is necessary that when you are preparing this instrument, you first insert the probe to know the depth of the anus so that what enters does not go deeper than it should and does not injure the patient; if the instrument is larger, cover the depth of the anus with cloths so that the instrument does not cause pain; put the funnel of the instrument on top, and moisten the instrument. When the boil opens and you can feel it with your hand, grasp its head with spatulas; when the buttocks are emptied, place moist compresses made from rose oil or green oil in the wound, placing the compress at the bottom of the anus and covering the anus and the wound with clean linen moistened in water or mallows that have been cooked; then treat it afterwards for two days with appropriate ointment until it is healed; sometimes lift the anus and the wound by irrigation with water and honey, then with water in which lily roots and long aristologia are cooked; then return to the ointment. If the wound closes in the anus, you must be careful not to cauterize with fire, but treat it as we have said previously in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	The midwife's first duty is to recognize the figure of natural childbirth, and the sign that it is time for a woman to give birth is when she begins pressing downwards and desires to smell the air: then the infant hastens to come out forthwith. Know this, that such childbirths are according to nature's figure, and the waters issue from above her head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, then press her belly gently so that the infant may come out quickly; for when it comes down upon its head, then is the afterbirth with it, and the womb is cleansed of its superfluities by good cleansing. But he who comes otherwise does not come naturally. For sometimes he comes upon his feet, and comes forth backside or belly upwards, or on his hands, or sometimes he comes belly upwards, or peradventure turned up by chance upon his neck, or in other unseemly figures; therefore it is necessary that the midwife be wise and skillful in these matters, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should aid her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes forth upon its head in natural fashion, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then make her sit down on a chair or let women hold her up; and arise her nature with oil of olive or fenugreek cooked, and then place the little spatumile between her thighs, of which form is thus:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And divide the afterbirth, and cut with your nail so much that the moisture which is within comes forth; and press down upon the woman's belly until the infant descends, and if it does not descend, then you must administer to the woman a clyster of ground fenugreek with oil of sesame. Then let her be sprinkled and sneezed upon with condiment, and hold her mouth and nose one hour: now the infant will come forth. And if both hands come out first, then you must press them gently little by little; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet up high; then overturn the chair upon the ground, and take care that the woman does not fall with the overturning; and if the hands cannot be entered, and the infant dies, then cut off the hands at the wrist which is here placed beforehand, and draw forth the child, and press it gently equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	If the infant comes forth upon its feet:
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the infant comes forth upon its feet, then you must raise it up;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it little by little until it is equal (in position);
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then seize one of its feet and stretch it out little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps up to the knees, then command her to seize (the infant) and let her sneeze with condiment;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it leaps forth, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then turn it little by little until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will come forth easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take ground althea, and oil of sesame, and molten gum, and grind all together in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	"And place upon the nature of woman within this ointment."
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	"Then make her sit in hot water up to below the ribs;"
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	"And once she is moistened beneath, place a collar of myrrh upon her and leave it for an hour."
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	"Then make her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and restrain her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child is now ready to leap."
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	"of the birth of the child onto her knees"
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	"When the child comes in this manner, then let him put his hands gently and gently;"
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	"then support her on her neck, and let the feet hang down, and let her lie on a bed;"
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	"and gently fold her hands together, then place them on the belly, and remove the cushions beneath until she is positioned correctly downward;"
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	"and if the child does not leap, then take her feet and shake her vigorously, then shake the belly upward, then place your hands;"
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	"And pull out the child gently; and command the woman to press down until the child emerges."
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	"of the birth of the child that comes from the womb with one hand held back;"
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	"I must contrive to bring back the hand:"
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	"if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman stand up and walk around;"
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	"If she cannot walk, then make her lie on a bed, and forcefully open her legs;"
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	"then prepare the mucus membrane that I have described;"
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	"And if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, and then try to bring back the hand;"
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	"And pull out the child according to its natural shape, and make her sneeze, then command her to press down until the child emerges completely."
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	"of the birth of the child onto its neck with hands spread out and face turned towards its mother's back;"
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	"The midwife must then seize her hand, gently turn it around and pull it out lightly;"
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	"And once it is aligned, place the prepared mucus membrane of olive oil and wax according to what we have said, then command her to move gently;"
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	"And once you have done this, make her sit on a chair and command her to press down; then make her sneeze."
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	"In the same manner for the afterbirth;"
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	"When it comes out completely like this with all of the afterbirth, then cut the umbilical cord with your fingernail until there is no more moisture;"
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	"And if the child's face and neck are bent down, then cut from the belly so that it is not retained and the child dies;"
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	"Then place the child back inside until you have positioned it correctly, then command the woman to press down gently once:"
adonques si istra legierement.	"then it will be born easily."
de l’issue des gemelz	"Concerning the birth of twins;"
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	"It should be known that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four; this is not uncommon."
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	"Two are rare and do not live long without nourishment;"
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	"I know this, that they can be multiplied, and those joined by the sac that divides them are separated by the caesarean section cut at the belly;"
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	"And sometimes they come out naturally just like any other child, as we have said."
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	"And if they cry when born, then care for them as we have said, and let the midwife be skillful, doing her work quickly and easily;"
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	"and do thus as is best for their health."
de plusors enfans	"Concerning multiple births;"
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	"It sometimes happens that there are one or two, three or four, five or six, seven or more up to fifteen formed in the womb, all perfectly shaped like children by the measure of God's glory;"
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	"and the midwife should know about this because such things can happen."
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	"So she should do what is necessary."
de l’enfant mort	Concerning a dead child:
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman for a dead child in the womb, as I have mentioned in the section on division, and no forceps emerge,
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	Then you must know whether the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fears death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	The woman should be positioned on her back, with her thighs inclined downward, and her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	And the minister shall tie the woman’s legs in two places, or secure them to the bed so that she cannot slip downward during delivery of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils made from althea and fennel and linseed, and anoint your hands with these same oils.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	Then gently insert your hand into the womb, then turn it once so that the loops are well-positioned.
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	And make sure that the child is presenting correctly, so that it descends headfirst.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	If the loops are positioned in its eyes, neck, mouth, palate, under the beard, or near the shoulders or ribs,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	And if delivery is occurring feet-first, then insert the hook or pin at the middle of the buttocks.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	And it is necessary that he hold the loop in his right hand and place the crook between the fingers of his left hand, and gently insert his whole hand. And he should then insert the loop into one of the places mentioned above until he reaches the empty space.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	And this is the shape of the loop:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then insert against one other peg, or two if necessary, so that the extraction is even.
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch it evenly by moving from one side to the other for it to come out, and make sure the pegs are teeth-like to hold it in place, like this:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if some part remains, let the physician anoint two of his fingers with oil and place them in that part, then pull on the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if nothing remains, then move this device to a higher position, and continue doing so until everything comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other and he cannot bring it back due to tension
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	Then you must wrap a cloth around it until all of it emerges
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	Then cut off the membrane at the joint of the sole or on the side and do likewise for the other hand, making two halves
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's thigh is large and it is narrow at the outlet where the bone is sharp at the end
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	Then you must place the spine of the spatula between your fingers, cut off the head and extract the splinter
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you can round it with an instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes along with the instruments that are next in the chapter
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	And do the same if the child has naturally large head
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	Then pull out the bones with pliers
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	And if the thigh bone comes out but is stuck in the socket, then split it until the ligaments that are at the hip joint come out
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	And if it still cannot come out, then cut it into pieces until you can remove it
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the ligaments are cut
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the attraction is light and the directions at the mouth of the uterus are easy
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is narrow in the belly or hip, then you must extract it using a cloth wrapped around your hand
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	And cut open the belly or hip until the ligaments that are there are severed
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	And if the other limbs are removed but the thigh si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	/
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	li tuant le col qu’el eschiet dunc a la crapaure
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	si vous voulez que je vienne pour vous aider à comprendre ce texte, n'hésitez pas à me le demander en mp
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	as li vous voulez que je vienne pour vous aider à comprendre ce texte, n'hésitez pas à me le demander en message privé !
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	Et si vous avez des questions sur la grammaire ou l’orthographe du patois, je peux vous aider aussi !
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	Pour tout problème de maths ou darithmetic, demandez à Dr. Wolf (en utilisant uniquement l'anglais pour les calculs avancés). Dr. Wolf va trouver la solution étape par étape 🔻
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if one has no power, then draw the fire by parts, and leave nothing of the secondine.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, let them bring what we have said before that comes into the marrow
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And if running with blood comes, then it should be placed in hot water restricting, and let them bring other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been killed, then she conceived another upon it, and the other was killed.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After many days, there appeared an abscess on his cheek, which swelled until it opened, and then began to discharge copiously.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned to the hospital, where I pondered long and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster with strong adhesion, from which came forth one bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I cleaned the wound and drew out many bones until the woman was much improved;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	And women would thus live for a long time, and sometimes a little bow of blood would come out.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I recorded this chapter earlier because, when the master encounters something unusual, he knows how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to reset the dislocation
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter follows the form of the compressor, with which the books are pressed; and it is made of two turns at the two ends of the two beams.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than the restrainer, and should be made of ebony or boxwood
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the wood should be one foot wide, and the edge of the beams one foot, and its length one and a half palms
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two beams there should be two supports of this same wood, which can be closed on both ends, each being half a palm or slightly more in length
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two supports are inserted into the mouth of the press to open it when the two horns are turned
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, resembling this one but more subtle and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood wood, according to the shape of the tongs
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and it should have at both ends two supports each, like you see here, one palm in length and two fingers wide
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	And when you wish to open the womb with all the instruments, have the woman sit on one bed, her feet hanging down and her legs opened
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then insert the two supports together into the womb and hold the head of the instrument under her thighs
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then open your hand on the entire instrument, just as you did with the tongs equally, according to the amount you wish to open the mouth of the womb, until the child comes out as it pleases her.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted and have many similar forms. When the physician has prepared them, he can work more quickly and can better satisfy men according to their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disregard any instrument until you have prepared it, for their necessity is not negligible.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the woman is retained in childbirth, you must command her to hold her breath and then make her sneeze with some powdered condurango, while covering her mouth and nose with your hands;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she sneezes because of it, so much the better
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take one pot and make a hole in the lid, then put herbs inside that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centory
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	and cook all these herbs or some of them in water in the pot over the fire. Then put one end of a tube into the hole of the pot and the other end into the mouth of the womb
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let it steam until the vapor comes inside the womb. Then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the woman expels quickly
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if after this treatment the woman remains and is not yet delivered, command her to wet her left hand in linseed oil or in white wax, then insert it into the vagina
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and search for the child; and when she finds it, grasp it gently and pull it straight out little by little, so that the womb does not tear during extraction
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but she must move it gently to the right and left and then pull; thus it will come out and be delivered.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the womb is very narrow, we have spoken about the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she does not deliver from all that we have said, be sure not to pull too hard
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but you must tie what is at the mouth of the womb to the woman's thigh, then give her an enema of treacle oil
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	and it will bring her relief and she will deliver; but nevertheless, when she delivers, if a bad smell comes to the stomach and head and affects the woman
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, suitable fumigations are necessary for this purpose: many of the ancients have proven that fumigation with watercress and dried figs is beneficial
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to fumigate women retained in labor or delivery is as follows
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	It resembles a tube made of glass, with the narrow end inserted into the vagina and the wider ends placed over the fire
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be done on hot coals, and continue until it is used up, then start another one
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born whose anus is not pierced but rather blocked by a small syphon
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore, the midwife must pierce this syphon with her thumb, but not with a sharp point, and be careful not to touch it with the nail
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place on linen moistened in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until it is clean
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you suspect that it may become blocked again, insert a lead tube into the opening and leave it in place for several days, then remove it when the child is ready to go to bed
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Sometimes this blockage comes suddenly from a wound or an aposteme (abscess); in such case cover the wound with a bandage and treat it as we have said for the lead tube
de la fistule dou fondement	of fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the anus are nodular and grow larger than those that come from near the anus or in the space of two fingers-width
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is one fistula or several; and when this nodular fistula is old, it opens, and becomes moist with thin white pus or thin bowels,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are persistent;
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that pierce up to the bladder,
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	"And thus one recognizes a fistula persistently discharging in the fundament, but not persistently:"
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	"and you put your two index fingers on the fundament and insert a thin needle of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity."
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	"And if it has tortuosity, then insert a thin probe of lead or a horse hair until you feel the probe or the hair with your finger;"
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	"and if you do not feel it and nothing comes out from the opening, whether by excretion or wind or water, as we have said:"
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	"You know that it does not pierce through; therefore hurry with the cure."
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	"And when the fistula persists down to the bladder or down to the passage of urine, so that urine squirts out and cannot be stopped by medication."
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	"If it has pierced as far as the hip joint, then the probe comes up to there;"
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	"if there is no tortuosity and the inflammation is around it, then it always goes towards the bowel, and neither medication nor soothing by ointment helps;"
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	"And in these persistently discharging fistulas there is no cure except surgery, and the vain boasting of foolish doctors who meddle with them."
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	"In that which is not persistent nor ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proved,"
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	"And let the patient lie on their stomach between your hands, and lift their legs up to their hips, and have their hips inclined towards their belly;"
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	"then insert a probe of brass or lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the probe comes out."
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	"If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you must put your two index fingers there,"
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	"then feel that the probe has pierced through; and if you feel between your fingers the wall of the bowel or flesh, then know that it is penetrating;"
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	"otherwise do not operate, for one cannot heal it."
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	"It is true that sometimes some can be healed, but this happens rarely;"
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	"And the aid that one does there is to heat the cautery carefully according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before;"
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	"And put it in hot into the fistula until it reaches near the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that those burned tissues have been cauterized, which resemble a feather;"
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	"And then use wet probes to clean it until that flesh comes out, then apply ointment externally soothing and healing."
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	"If it is healed in this way, good. If not, there is no other way to heal it;"
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	"And if the probe enters but does not reach your finger that is at the fundament, and there is a thick covering of flesh or bowel between your two fingers, and you see the fistula coming out from under this covering of the heart;"
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	"then cut off the beginning of the fistula, and put in the probe again, then apply the cautery afterwards until it reaches the tip of the probe;"
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	"and the probe will be freed and fall out; then clean off those burned tissues which resemble a feather, leaving nothing behind."
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	"And if your hand trembles and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with hot medicine."
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	"For the cautery of fire accomplishes two things: namely, the burning of those adjacent tissues, and the hemostasis of blood and the cooking of moisture;"
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	"then use wet probes to clean it or with crushed herbs until the wound gapes wide open, and burned flesh comes out from the bowel;"
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	"then treat the wound with healing ointments soothing to the skin, which are dry medicines."
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	"For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not return."
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	"And if the fistula comes from deep inside the fundament and is far away from the body, put your finger into the fundament and feel for it."
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	"If you feel the probe and there are two between your finger and the bowel or flesh where it is about to pierce, then do not hesitate to operate with confidence and hope through one of these three methods:"
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	"either cauterize it as we have said before, or cut it out entirely, or if you cannot do this, put probes in and clean it as at first;"
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	"but do not go too deep lest you cut the tissue that supports the fundament and cause incontinence without wanting to."
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	"then treat it as we have said;"
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	"maybe it will be healed by moving that covering away and cleaning it after it has been cut near the fundament with a probe or other pointed instrument;"
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	"then clean off that burned flesh in the wound as much as you can;"
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	"then try to close the wound and keep the fistula away from the fundament, which will be easier for the patient."
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	"And sometimes fistulas are like this: when you put in the probe and it is on the side of the fundament near the skin above;"
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	"then take a probe pierced at the tip like this:"
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	"And tie one thread around two places, and put the probe all the way into the fistula until it reaches the tip."
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	"If it is passing through the margin of the fundament inside, then pull out the thread from that hole, so that you put your finger into the fundament;"
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	"and tie the end of the thread and bring the two holes together and bind them tightly to each other, leaving it for one or two days;"
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	"And tighten it again sometimes until the thread cuts through those tissues between them and falls off;"
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	"then treat the wound until it is healed and closed."
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	"If the fistula does not open on its own, then make it open in every way that you can, if it is not too deep."
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"For it is not necessary to cut so deeply for the closure and then treat it as we have said until it heals."
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	"The shape of the spinal needle used to open a fistula is very sharp and pointed at one end;"
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	"and the other end is not pointy so that you do not cut what you should not cut, as you can see here:"
des emorroydes	"hemorrhoids"
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	"Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the fundament like grains of resin, and there are small ones and large ones, and blood always flows from them;"
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	"and there is one or more of them outside the fundament or at the tip of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture;"
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	"and they are always covered with a little yellowish water or a little blood, and they have the color of flesh;"
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	"And the treatment for those who have hemorrhoids inside the fundament is that you tell the patient to go to a privy and strain until they come out of the fundament and then the threads will appear;"
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	"then hurry up and grasp it with forceps or hold it between your fingers, and cut its roots;"
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	"and if the pincers cannot grasp them due to their moisture, then take them with a cloth or cotton or a piece of chamois leather;"
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	Remove the hairs on your two legs, then trim them, and apply some warm powders in place of a cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is described in the chapter on cauterization, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	And if the fundament cannot pass out, then administer to the patient a purging enema with sharp and bitter medicine to wash what is in the fundament so that it can exit freely.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	If the patient is able to pass the stool by themselves, and if the feces are outside of the fundament, then the treatment is simple
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And it is necessary to grasp them with your fingernail or forceps, and trim them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and so that the patient fears incision with a knife
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary to prepare the suture in this manner: take one twisted thread, insert it into a needle, and then pull the thread upwards and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and make the thread tight, then tie the knot and remove the needle, and do this for all of them, leaving one to draw up any excess blood
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place over the fundament one damp cloth moistened in rose oil or wax, and put it on the fundament, and command the patient to rest
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and leave him until he passes stools, and when they are passed, treat them with ointment and other treatments until they are healed
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	on the drying of fecal matter on the fundament
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying of feces in the intestines, and this occurs due to constriction of nature, especially when the patient is elderly or when medication is ineffective
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you use the tip of a spatula or your fingernail to gently scrape off the dried feces on top without wetting it
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	Then treat him until he is healed as it should be.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	And if he cannot heal, then resume the cauterization more intensely than before, until he recovers greatly and is scarred.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat him until he is healed.
dou fremit	fever
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	An ant is a small, four-legged creature that lives inside the body and moves about very quickly;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes it finds him cold, and he feels it just like death from trembling, and it comes throughout the body, more to the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a feather of a goose wing or a strong vulture feather and place it on the trembling so that the circles encompass the trembling all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then twist your hand around the whole feather until you grasp all around the trembling and thrust it in deep, and uproot the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit to do so with a feather of iron or steel according to this form, and it should be thin underneath and tapering at the tip
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	then do not pierce it, so that you can hold both (feathers) together and press them; And if you wish to cauterize the trembling, then do so as it is written in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of a clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes they make a clyster of silver or lead, or molten brass or hammered metal; And sometimes they make them of these instruments small and large according to those for whom they are intended
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those which are prepared for the treatment of children and those who are weak and feeble should be small
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small or large clyster is as follows: wide where the belly is bound in this manner
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there should be an opening where the belly is bound, as you see here, and the excrement should be pierced within; And it should have two holes on one side and one hole on the other
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly where one places the medicines should be made of an animal bladder or parchment, and pierced all around with small holes,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	"Place a piece of thick cloth between each hole, then insert into these holes one strong thread made from twisted yarn, bent in the shape of a '10' or whatever suits best around it, and bring together the belly like a goat."
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	"And when the medication is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then perform a clyster; and this is the shape of the circle:"
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	"And let the medication not be too hot nor too cold, and grease the tip of the clyster with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently."
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	"Then the minister squeezes with both hands together until it is entirely empty, then remove the clyster, and the patient lifts his legs at the bedside,"
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	"And if the medication wants to come out, hold it back as much as possible; and if he sleeps all night like this, then there is greater help."
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if you perform a clyster on someone with abdominal descent disease, and the medication rushes to come out, then begin again until it is finished."
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	"And if hemorrhoids are present in the fundament or an abscess, then the clyster should be as subtle as for a child;"
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	"and this is the shape of the subtle clyster when the skin is stretched tight:"
des plaies	"of wounds"
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	"We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medications according to their fulfillment."
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	"I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to where the wounds are made, and of what they are made."
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	"The things by which wounds are made are by striking with a stone, cutting with a sword and dagger, or with a spear or staff or similar things;"
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	"or they are made according to the location on the body, such as wounds that fall on the neck, or on the head, or the face, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;"
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	"And I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and will begin with simple head wounds, because the memory will come in its chapter."
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	"I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, one should take care if it was caused by striking with a stone or similar things, and if the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large,"
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	"and you should quickly lift a hot swelling: perform the cephalic cautery immediately if there is little blood coming from the wound, and the cautery should be applied on the opposite side of the wounded part;"
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	"and avoid overfeeding the patient with wine and fatty foods."
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	"And if it cannot be cauterized, then reduce his food and drink, and let him not drink wine nor eat meat;"
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	"and put on the wound, if a hot swelling appears, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in stiptic wine;"
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	"and if there is no hot swelling, then put powder on the wound while it still has all its blood and before it is touched by air, which I will describe later;"
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"and if the air has already touched it, then apply some ointments until it is healed."
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	"And if the wound is large, such as from a sword cut or similar things, and the lips cannot be brought together by tension, then bring them together by stitching, as I will describe for abdominal wounds."
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	"If the wound is exposed to the bone and gapes, and holds only by a little, then cut it off; then treat the wound with medications, and replace hard flesh in place of skin."
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	"and order the patient to eat fatty foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, also poultry and similar things."
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	"And if you find rottenness in the skin, but it has not yet reached the bone, then cut off all the rotted part and throw away the gangrene, then treat the wound;"
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	"and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be stopped by medications, then find the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread;"
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	"and if that does not help, then cauterize it."
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	"And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy: you should put in this powder that seals before the air touches it."
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	"The way to make the powder is: take incense in one part, dragon's blood in two parts, and quicklime in three parts, and grind it finely;"
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	"and apply the powder to the wound, pressing it firmly until it adheres well and joins together with all its blood;"
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	"then bind it well, and leave it undisturbed until it is healed, because the medication should not be removed until the wound is healed."
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	"Sometimes this is also done with quicklime alone when incense and dragon's blood are not available, but before the air touches the wound."
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	"And if the air has already touched the wound, especially in summer, then do not put this powder on it;"
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	"but apply some digestive ointments or poultices made of barley flour with water and honey until it softens;"
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	"then treat it with other treatments until it is healed."
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	"And if the bone is broken along with the wound, and the wound is small, then extract it with fine forceps;"
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	"and I will tell you about head fractures later."
de la plaie dou col	"of the wound on the neck"
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	"If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between that and one on the head, except if the nerve of the neck or an artery is cut."
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	"If it's the nerve, there is nothing else to do but leave it alone and apply nothing restrictive, because that harms the nerves and causes them to withdraw;"
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	"and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member;"
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	"but the medication should be warm, such as hot water mixed with rose oil and cooked water also mixed with hot water;"
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	"and other medicaments according to this method, and moist ointments."
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the wound is large, then stitch it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals."
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	"And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, then open them lower down;"
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	"and if an artery is cut and bleeding comes forth, then uncover it, tie it off, and cauterize it if necessary;"
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	"and if the spine of the neck or the heart is cut, but the passage is preserved through which food goes,"
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	"then stitch up the heart to the windpipe of the neck, and do not touch the windpipe itself but replace it according to its natural shape;"
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	"then bind it carefully and leave it for a few days before treating it with drying ointments until it heals."
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	"And if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then find it;"
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	"and if there are pieces of bone, remove them all that you can, and leave those that you cannot have until the wound rots;"
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let the dislocation be reduced and bound
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as described in its chapter
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of wounds from spears or knives
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a blow from a spear or knife and the wound is deep, then observe whether air enters the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep and is full of fresh blood throughout, then do not put the powder in at first nor bind it so that the blood does not be drawn down into it
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and let it return to the heart and kill the patient
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but put an attractive ointment on it and bind it twice a day
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have ointment, then put in the wound old cotton to suck out the moisture
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and let the patient lie on the wound for three days or four, or more
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	so that there comes no spasm nor trembling of the heart nor twitching of the lungs
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see these signs, then know that the wound is saved
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Therefore treat it with tents and other treatments until it is healed
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal nor close up, then know that there is a fistula; so treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife and it is simple, either before or behind, then treat it as those that are in front
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, suture it; and if it is small, apply powder to it. And if it is close up against the bone and has cut off pieces of it, then scrape out the wound and treat those fragments separately if they are disjointed
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not disjointed, then leave the wound to fester until the fragments come loose
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for wounds on other members, the judgment is as we have said
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the abdomen is great, moderate, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	Sometimes, during a large wound, an intestine or part of it protrudes outwards.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and stitching is more difficult, sometimes even small wounds are worse than large ones,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	Because if one resets [the dislocation] without placing the intestines back in, or not doing so heat by heat;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	For when the intestines swell due to coldness they do not return unless reset,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	And therefore it is good to move the lesser wound, so that when one resets the intestines to their place, they may be like the others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly happens in four ways
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The two common sutures occur at the suture of the abdomen,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	"And the sewing of other wounds on the body, with two others proper, are common to other wounds."
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	"But nevertheless they are more specific when it comes to abdominal stitches, and I will discuss each one and explain them."
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	"I say that when the wound is small, nothing of the intestine has come out,"
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	"and if it does not require anything else to be put back in place, this can be done in one of two ways:"
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	'Or because the wound is small, as we have said,'
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	'Or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.'
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	"And when it is cold, heat it in this manner:"
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	"Wet a sponge or a soft cloth in hot water only,"
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	"Or you could cook it in boiling water with salt and pepper,"
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	"And raise the intestines until the swelling is gone;"
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	"Then apply this binding wine and be careful not to squeeze too hard while tying it."
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	"And when you see the swelling disappearing, then moisten the intestines with warm water in which salt and mulberries have been cooked,"
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	"For by this means the entrance to the wound is widened somewhat;"
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	"And if it cannot enter, then make a small incision into the wound using an instrument used for tying hemorrhoids."
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	"And the first treatment is to be careful not to cut too deeply,"
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	"That no one should cut without there being a great necessity;"
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	"This is the instrument used for splitting it open:"
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	"So cut inside the curve and don't follow the skin, and here you can see its shape:"
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	"And when the wound is widened and the intestines have come out,"
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	"Then gently push them back into place according to their natural shape and proper position;"
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	"If you can manage it, for this is important."
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	"When the wound is large and it is located below the belly,"
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	"It is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back;"
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	"And place his legs higher than his head;"
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	"And if it is located below the belly,"
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	"Then raise the head and chest above the lower parts;"
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	"And also, if the abdominal wound is in one of the two buttock regions,"
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	"Then make sure that the wounded part is higher than the other."
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	"And thus you must arrange things as I have said for large and medium-sized wounds."
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	"For small wounds, use what has been prepared;"
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	"Then have between your hands one of your assistants who will gently wipe the entire wound with his hand,"
et assemble les levres;	And join together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	And this is the common way of sewing
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	And you must take a needle or several ones, according to the quantity of the width of the wound.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave two inches of space from the head of the wound and insert a needle with a good strong thread attached to it;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the needle
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	that is underneath the skin inside, until you make it pierce through to that side
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and bring together the two heads of the needle together with the four;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then wrap a doubled thread around the needle on both sides
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then bring together the two heads of the wound in front
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave two inches of space and insert another needle
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie it with thread as you did the first needle
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and continue to do this according to how many needles are needed
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the entire wound is restrained
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be medium-sized, between thin and thick
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for thin needles pierce all the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter well enough
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	that is why they must be medium-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	do not push the needles too deep into the flesh and skin
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	for they would pierce and open up the wound ahead of the suture.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	then cut off the heads of the needles so that they do not bother the sick person while sleeping
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and place tents or bandages over the heads of the needles to hold them in place
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them there until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of suturing with needles is more useful for small wounds
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for it takes only one needle or two
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second suture is common
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	And you should join the two skins of leather and the two skins of sinew together with one needle having one strong medium thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	And when you have pierced these joints together
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and bend the needle back to where you started, in the manner of cutting cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	Place the thickness of a large finger joint between each stitch;
ceste costure sevent li home,	This stitch is for men
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	I sewed a wound that a man had in his belly
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was stabbed with a knife
