et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's width long
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	And it gushed out of his intestines for over two palms' length
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I put his intestines back in after he had been out of them for 24 hours
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was healed by the 15th day and it cured well
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, but this was a miracle
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	I did not treat it with any ointment or medicine because I was in a place where none could be found
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And I put on old cotton twice a day and washed the wound with honey water until it healed
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now, I will tell you two proper ways to stitch:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and insert it from outside towards inside
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it has pierced the heart directly, then lift up the skin or flesh where you inserted the needle
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	And make it pierce from inside towards outside in another place
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	The purpose of this stitch is that you sew just like a furrier sews furs
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And leave the skin once on one side and take it up again on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way to stitch, as Galen says properly,*
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	If this occurs as some do, who join the two parts together naturally
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one shoulder blade to the other in such a way that
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	Stick a needle at the head of the navel near by, and pierce that spot only.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the thread protruding.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle around, and pierce it from the front part to the inside one
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the two ends of the thread
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce both of them from the front part to the inside one, in two other navel holes that are opposite each other.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the proper way to suture and the most common method.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien says this word, and some testify it
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must place one needle on this side and the other on that side, in the manner of those who sew hides
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the wound is inside the belly
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	the stitching is more difficult than other wounds on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the art has moved it
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	put back the intestines and the skin, then put the powder around the flesh
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the wound has moved, put on some ointment that is available, until the wound is healed.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and sew up the stitches, and the navel.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as you would others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	And if you do not have any medicine, then put on cotton wool as soon as the wound begins to heal
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For in many cases, when wounds are simple, you have no need of any other medicine besides
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the principal members
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary for you to moisten a light linen in warm oil of roses, or rose oil
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the angles and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if there is pain or corruption in the bowels, which happens many times,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	If black wine enemas are applied, and especially if putrefaction reaches the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierces it internally, know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	"And it is due to the narrowness of the veins there,
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the serpent jumps from the wound, then push it back just like the intestine while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become worms or black, then you must tie the area that is black so that no bleeding occurs.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut off what is between the ligature
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put two strips of cloth hanging down from below the wound until far enough to tie them around the extraction when the serpent falls, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the bowel is ruptured but the wound is small
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some cases
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	for I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and both digestion and wind passed through it;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it according to what I could do, and did not stop until he was healed and the wounds were closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his belly
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	but there was no pain, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some surgeons said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take threads with large knots, then bring together the edges of the wound
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the thread has opened the mouth, put it on both lips
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it pulls its mouth open;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	then cut off its head so that it cannot untie itself.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another thread afterwards in the same manner as before until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This stitch will hold in the intestine and there will be no harm to the patient;
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	Take the end of this intestinal thread that is very well cleaned,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie a fine twisted linen thread at the end of this intestinal thread;
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread through the needle and sew up the intestine where it is torn.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this method of stitching with threads is no further than according to the way of safety and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no help nor health but through subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or ulcer, when it becomes inflamed, is universally called a "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	especially when it is healed over and sinks back.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is truly according to the truth: a hard, white nodule that does not cause pain
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also healed over like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And sometimes it forms a clear round bulge, and other times it becomes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes it is small, and other times quite large;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	"And I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not clean, and there is no scar,"
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	"is only visible due to one of the eight causes:"
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	"That is to say, due to the smallness of blood or flesh;"
ou por sa malice;	"or because of its evil nature;"
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	"or because there is hard scar tissue inside and on the lips that does not allow new skin to form;"
ou il i a trop de bowe;	"or because of too much bowing;"
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	"or because the place is blocked off and the material is of poor quality;"
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	"or because the medication used in treatment was not good;"
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	"or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence."
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	"or because in this region digestion is slow and recovery takes time due to its natural tendency towards inflammation;"
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	"or because there are veins or bones present:"
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	"And I have already demonstrated all of these causes, and the signs, and the treatments with medications in the relevant division."
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	"Now I must tell you about the treatment for a fistula that is done through manual labor."
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	"Know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body;"
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	"for there are fistulas which come from large veins and arteries, and from nerves,"
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	"or from the sinus, or the intestines, or the bladder, or from any of the ribs,"
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	"or from the spine of the back, or from any joint in the hands or feet;"
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	"And there are even some that come from the principal member itself and similar locations."
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	"And all fistules of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and skill involved;"
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	"and if there is any fistula that does not come from the places I have mentioned, you may be confident about its treatment,"
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	"And recognize it, then take a tent of copper or iron, and if the fistula is straight, insert it;"
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	"and if the fistula is crooked, seek a thin lead tent,"
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	"for lead can bend more readily around its curvature;"
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	"And if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search it well with tents,"
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	If one performs an enema through one of the openings
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because moisture flows from one opening to another, clearing them out;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then search thoroughly using all your strength to determine if there is any bone or nerve there, and insert the hook deeply
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when you press on their hand, and where exactly they feel it
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and once you truly know where the pain is located, whether it is away from the joint, nerve, artery, or vein
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the locations that I have mentioned, then operate according to what I have told you
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the fracture and rotten splinters within it.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	then dress the wound until it is healthy
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is very deep in its proper place, you should operate deeply until you can go no further
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then insert wet lint into boiling hot water, and bring it up to the mouth of the fistula
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medication burns away the excess matter remaining at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply dressings of clean lint until it is healed
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it does not heal from that, then cauterize it as we have said
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves do not trouble you in the main limbs, as we have said
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, scrape it until all the corruption is removed
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then dress with clean lint until it heals
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it does not heal, then repeat the operation as before
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	Know that you have not yet reached the bottom:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you uncover and search until you reach the bottom
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all of the corruption, then close up the wound.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is healed thus, that's good
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	therefore there is nothing else to do but leave it to nature
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small piece of bone corrupted, and you can grasp it with forceps
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then extract it using one of the instruments suitable for this purpose
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many pieces of bone, break them all up and leave not one behind
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture is causing trouble and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	"If there is bone and moisture and flesh, deliver the bones."
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place on the wound something that prevents putrefaction.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the flesh has rotated completely around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And then they will move the bones more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	And if it is a large bone, such as the thighbone or shinbone,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	If you merely scrape away the corruption until all of the blackness is gone,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	"And if there is much corruption of its parts, it reaches even to the bone:"
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	"Then it should be sewn up all around the corruption, and then healed until it is solid:"
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	"And I will tell you about a fistula that happened in one man's leg,"
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	"So that you can take an example from it and help in your work."
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	"He was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg due to some cause that came from inside the body,"
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	"So much so that matter came to the leg and it was swollen with an large abscess, and had no visible reason to open,"
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	"But the doctors foolishly tried so hard to make the abscess open,"
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	"That they corrupted much matter, and it became a fistula with many holes that all poured out and moistened from inside the body;"
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	"And many doctors tried to heal it for about two years, but there was no wisdom in their art of hands,"
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	"So I was called and went to see his leg and the remedies they were using,"
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	"And I saw that what flowed from the holes was very foul."
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	"and the young man's flesh became red and had a yellowish hue."
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	"I plugged one of these holes with a wisp of cloth, and then searched for all the other holes,"
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	"And found that some holes were opposite each other on every side of the leg."
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	"So I hurried and cut into one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone,"
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	"I found it rotten and perforated, and the corruption extended to the bone inside."
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	"I saw what appeared to me to be decay of the bone, and I thought that there was no other decay besides what I removed;"
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	"And I began to dress the wound with dry medicines over a long period of time, but it would not heal;"
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	"And then I recommenced, and discovered the bone just as before,"
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	"I found that the bone was still corrupt, and scraped it, and then removed it, and I worked to heal the spot;"
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	"but I could not do so because the bone had grown around the palm of my hand, and was drawn taut over its entire surface,"
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	"then I dressed it with medicine, and it healed quickly and completely."
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	"and there was no need to recommence the operation except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it,"
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	"And because I feared death for him."
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	"For although he often bled from the evacuation, he was healed completely,"
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	"And in place of the bone there grew hard flesh, and he was well disposed, and suffered no harm nor misfortune throughout his whole body, neither then nor afterwards."
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	"And if any bone in the body is broken, it should be set in this manner:"
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	"Take one linen cloth, and stretch it across the head of the exposed bone,"
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	"And command someone to pull it upwards;"
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	"And take another thicker linen cloth than the first one and tie it over the flesh that covers the bone,"
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	"and stretch the head so that you may draw out the corrupt flesh from underneath;"
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	"And uncover the flesh over the spot where you wish to break it, so that the bone does not bruise the flesh;"
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	"And place a hot iron or a heated metal plate under the bone to burn away the corrupt flesh;"
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	"And it must be done until one can see and feel that the corruption is entirely gone, and then once more."
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	"And if the bone is corrupted but not exposed, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,"
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	If all flesh is laid bare; then place one coal underneath
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then bind the two parts together using corruption, and let the bandage be as long as the corruption itself, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupted joint and bind the bone on the other side that contains it;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption extends over two joints, there is nothing else to do but cut
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if the corruption is at the wrist of the hand or foot, it is a very difficult thing
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nevertheless you must inquire about this corruption how it affects
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way that you can, but without harming the veins or nerves.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	know that many incisions and bandages are needed to cut these bones according to their arrangement and appearance
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and thinness, and their length and shortness, and their hardness
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	Therefore one must prepare each tool according to its function
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you which tool you will need, according to your knowledge of this art
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	Therefore consider the tool that you need according to what is appropriate for it.
dou feu	Fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	Flesh putrefies either from causes within or from causes without.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have treated this corruption with medications and yet they do not benefit
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cut off that member up to the place where the corruption comes from
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the sick person escapes death either by amputation or by the lesser evil of losing the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	And the sign is when the member becomes black as if it had been burned with fire
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness comes putrefaction, which then spreads from limb to limb
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and spreads throughout the body. So hasten to amputate
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	And if it is due to the bite of venomous beasts such as sea scorptions, snakes, and similar ones
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corruption is at the top of the arm, cut off the arm without sparing the hand from being affected.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, cut it off at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it reaches the arm, cut it off at the elbow. If it passes beyond the elbow, then death is certain.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And no external remedies will avail unless they are used in large enough quantities
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And similarly when corruption comes to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cut off after the second joint
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes onto the foot, cut off the entire foot
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up into the leg, cut off at the knee joint
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the sick person die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	And the method of amputating or cauterizing a limb is as follows: tie it above and below the point where you intend to cut
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister's hand downwards towards the lower ligature, and another minister's hand upwards towards the upper ligature
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and uncover the flesh between the two ligatures with one broad spatula until the bone is exposed
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or cauterize it, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the cautery does not touch the healthy area
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and prevent other wounds and blisters from forming on the sick person.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs while you are operating, cauterize the area immediately
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or apply some restrictive powders. Then continue with your treatment until it is complete
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then tie the wounded limb with a suitable ligature and treat it until it heals
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I shall tell you what happened to one man concerning his big toe
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He had a blackness that seemed like it had been burned by fire
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and the corruption came first to his right foot and then spread throughout the entire foot
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corruption, he quickly cut off his foot and was healed
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and some time later, the corruption returned to the index finger of his hand, and he came to me
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I applied percussion remedies after cleansing his body but could not stop the corrosion
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to because I had hope that I could remove the matter through percussion treatment.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	I was also afraid that if I cut off his hand, he would die
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the strength of the man was weak. And he despaired entirely and returned home.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	"And he hastened to cover his hand, and was healed;"
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	"And I have not said this except because one should do otherwise when it is necessary."
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an ulcer appears on the skin and stays there for so long that it forms a large boil.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then it reddens and bursts open, and the boil jumps out, leaving an empty space like a hollow vessel
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is as thin as finely-woven silk.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	And it does not go down to the bone or to the nerve, and such illness is called "shallow."
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it extends so far that it reaches the bone and goes deep, then it is called a "fistula."
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And the skin is such that if you cut that skin all around, even when it is thin like cloth
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and yet it does not smell because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you think that the skin smells and the corruption is not deep
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	then treat it with a clyster like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look to see if the breast is large and the boil that is on it has a foul odor
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then use a clyster made of Egyptian medicine made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take equal parts of psyllium and oil and litharge, and put them in one vessel on the fire
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	And then take some of it according to your need, and mix it with water and honey
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use it as a clyster for the breast, and squeeze the opening tight;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing it out
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times until the breast is healed and the odor is gone.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	And sometimes you should clyster with water of ashes
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and take some ashes from vine wood, and pour water on it
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then strain it and use it as a clyster until you know that the breast is well cleaned.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	And if the patient cannot tolerate this, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then use a clyster of water and honey with a little bit of crushed litharge in it
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or use a clyster of honey and mead mixed wine that has the property to cleanse and wash
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and makes the flesh swell;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	And when you have done this, and you are sure that the breast is well cleaned,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	If the clyster causes flesh to be born there.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And it is that you take emplaustum diaphnit, and they do this with rose oil in wine
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	Or you clyster it with certain medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken the properties or treatment of ointments
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	And if the opening in the breast is small, and the tube of the clyster cannot enter
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	If you widen it a little with an iron tool, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basilicon ointment until it is widened
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	And if the wound is too wide, then close it and leave only one finger or where the clyster can enter
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the hole that throws bowels is above, lower it a little below
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is deep, do not allow flesh to enter
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	Then prepare it in such a way that the bowel runs to the lowest point it is at
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the bowel is deep, do not allow flesh to enter
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	Then prepare it in such a way that the bowel runs gently downwards, and do not leave anything of the bowel there
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	And take medicines that are consolidative to put on the breast
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	And let it rest on one linen cloth which covers all the breast
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	Then close as tightly as possible around the opening in the breast, a little larger than the first
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	Then let soft ointment be on one other cloth according to the quantity of the opening
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	And put it on the opening in the breast to alleviate the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth outside, except once after many days
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And that which is on the opening of the breast, remove often to remove the bowel
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And know what comes from the bowel, whether it is venomous or little or enough, digested or undigested
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	And beware if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	And when this medicine has been applied in such a way that you see the nature that comes out of the opening of the breast
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	Then know that the breast has already healed, and approaches health
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	And then untie it in the morning or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Then change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast throws undigested bowel after many days, know that the breast has not healed yet.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons come out afterwards for a long time, do not despair of health
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For health approaches. For there are men to whom it takes a long time for flesh to enter their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if undigested bowel comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast has not healed yet.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	And if the breast is slow to heal and is far from recovery, then apply medicines that are drying in substance and dry in power
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as diaphoretic ointment, for it contains much vitriol, and this is the last medicine
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take a diaphoretic ointment, made with rose oil, and add an equal amount of old wine by weight;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	Then cook it and use it; and this same thing done better cooked and thickened;
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	When there are no diaphoretic ointments present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloe and frankincense, grind them up, and powder them over honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	Then put one cloth into it and put it on the breast, and sometimes administer aristologus drink
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of heavenly lily, which is also like wheat flour and lentil flour.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	And use simple or compound medicines: grind them up, make powder, and put on the honey I mentioned earlier, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the illness is prolonged and not cured by this treatment
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	Then know that the corruption has gone deep, causing inflammation in the bone or hard members or ligaments
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If the treatment for fistula is like we have said earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil on the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panaritium is a boil that arises under the nail of the finger of the hand
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or foot, or sometimes arises in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	And when it becomes infected, if no attention is paid to it, then one great boil appears
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they will continue to grow and swell until they reach the root of the nail, and perhaps cover the whole thing
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and corrosion spreads to the bone causing a foul-smelling pain, and the skin around it is red and swollen with a yellowish hue
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When treated as described in this section, but the treatment has no effect
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then you must cut away all the excess nail tissue that remains
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauterization is very helpful if the bone and nail are healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	And if the nail presses on the flesh, and begins to prick it, causing a wound.
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you must place a bandage under the nail that is pricking the flesh
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and raise it up, cutting away that delicate and light skin.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on top of the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply dressings until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is on the bone, cut it off and scrape it out, because as long as the corrupted bone remains there, it cannot heal
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see that two are corrupting, cut them both off just as was said before
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then dress it until it heals.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is wounded and swollen, causing great pain, you must first cleanse it
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut off the nail from the spur bone sharply in a diagonal cut
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be sure that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from the wound of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	Some men may have two joints that are entirely fleshy
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is some bone present and at other times there is no nail
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some grow from the root of the joint, where they are found between certain fingers
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that arise on any of the joints of the fingers do not move
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that arise at the joint of the finger sometimes move
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The cutting of one that is entirely fleshy is easy in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born from the root of the joint is difficult to heal: be careful with him.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	For one who is born or moves backwards at night, first cut the flesh evenly up to the bone
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut the bone with an appropriate knife and cure it until it is clean.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations that come together at both sides come from birth, or from the welding of a wound, or from burning by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	Therefore you must cut that fusion so that the limbs return to their natural shapes
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between them moistened cloths or bandages soaked in rose oil so that they do not fuse together
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between both thin slices of lead until the limbs are fused as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If dislocations come to any of his limbs with the palm, cut that fusion appropriately
Des vils	Worms
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Worms are large and swollen bags full of melancholic humors that come to many limbs of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And they occur more often in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you must administer to him some times a purge of bile, and then cleanse him with the holy water.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron is done in two ways: one is to cut them and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is to lift up the swelling and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision is done in this manner: first raise the leg with hot water very strong until the thick blood becomes subtiliated,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then hold the patient's leg above the hip down to the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then cut the vein in one, two, or three places with a wide incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then remove and draw out the black blood with your hand from one end to the other until as much blood comes out as the patient can tolerate.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then the clot, and tell him to wrap himself in warm flesh-colored cloth.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	"and restart the evacuation and bleeding when veins are full, harming the patient."
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	"The raising of the leg is done in this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,"
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then places it in a bath and raises the leg with warm water until it becomes red and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire and then place the leg against the vein from the long bone to the top of the knee joint or below the ankle joint;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then bind it with the skin of an ox and scrape the vein from each side until it becomes visible when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters into the skin it seems like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then place the knife under it until it is raised from the skin, then pinch it lightly with the ox's horn;
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then cut it in one other place three fingers away; then scrape off the skin over the vein until it appears
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it with the razor, as you have done, and sew it to another one, as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then make another incision, or several if necessary, then lift it up and cut it at the two ends of the foot
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then draw it out and lift it up as far as the second incision; then pull it out incision by incision until it is all out, then cut it
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	And if you cannot draw it out and lift it, then insert a needle with a strong doubled thread
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and pull it out, and put your hand under the vein, turning it from side to side until it comes out
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	Make sure it does not break, for if it breaks you will not be able to pull it out or lift it up, causing harm to the patient
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once you have pulled it all out, place on the wound moist wool soaked in wine and rose oil until it is clean.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is constricted and twisted upon itself and not straight as we have said
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	Then you must cut it crookedly but do not break it; then pull it out as we have said before
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the blade used to cut the vein is curved and does not cut straight so that it does not break the vein
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it should be of thick curvature, for if it were thin it would cut the vein but it should be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the saphenous vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in legs, in warm regions where there are no herbs or trees, and on dry ground without moisture
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, which happens due to corruption that comes from under the skin
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	like how it occurs inside the body with worms and veins that appear between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there appears a very great inflammation in the leg
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the location changes and the vein begins to protrude like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the skin opens, you must wrap around it a piece of lead weighing from one and a half to two pounds and tie it
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the lead hang down on the leg; whenever any more comes out, wrap it around the lead and tie it again
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a portion of it, wrap the remaining part around the lead, but do not cut it at its root until it has all come out
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will retreat into the flesh and cause an abscess and corruption in that location, causing a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore, it must be pulled out little by little until its end, so that nothing remains inside the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein is as long as five or ten palms when it has been pulled out
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and once a man came to me whose vein was twenty palms long; when you cut it, it makes one hole or more and pierces through to the bottom
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; empty the matter that is inside and apply medications that prevent corruption to the location for a few days, then treat it like other abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it opens at the ankle or foot
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there are many holes from which veins sprout forth; therefore treat them as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that appear between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease" because it often affects oxen
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that appears between skin and flesh and goes throughout the body moving up and down
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	"and he feels it well as he moves limb to limb,
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	"And it is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, such as they come forth like worms and serpents in the belly;"
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	"And doubt arises from its evilness because when it goes through the body towards the head, it reaches the eye,"
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	"perhaps it enters and destroys the eye; this happens many times."
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	"And when you see him being cured and drawn forth, nothing can be done until it goes away:"
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	"therefore one must tie the joint above and below with a strong, tightly drawn bandage,"
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	"then cut open on top and draw it forth; if the worm is buried deeply in the flesh, you will not find it,"
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	"If so, cauterize with fire until it dies."
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	"And the greatest harm that it causes is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;"
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	"And if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, press down tightly beneath it with a needle, then cut open above and draw it forth;"
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	"It is necessary to use medications for bodily purification to dissolve putrid humors,"
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	"And if he has eaten corrupted meats."
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	"About the pain that comes from windiness"
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	"This disease is called in our land ' vakir', and it is a pain that comes into certain members,"
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	"and then it moves from member to member; this I have seen with mine own eyes."
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	"I was called to see a woman who was sick, and she showed me her arm where there was a small swelling in the vein of the forearm;"
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	"And soon after I saw it rise up like a worm towards the shoulder,"
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	"More swiftly than anything, just like live silver when it flows from one place to another;"
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	"The pain leaves that place and sticks in the shoulder,"
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	"and then a little while after it spreads throughout the body until it reaches the other arm;"
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	"Then she said that it was turning around her body again, just as I saw it."
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I wondered greatly how the member could move about so from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness behave in such a way."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	"Still, I had often heard that pain can well move from one place to another,"
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	"I had never seen it like this in the woman."
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	"and I thought that perhaps it was because the woman had a thin body and her veins were exposed,"
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	"which caused that constrained windiness to appear;"
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	"And this is not apparent in those who are delicate and have moist bodies with concealed veins."
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	"When you see someone being cured from this illness, if the patient feels that pain which we have spoken of,"
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	"The swelling above and below will quickly appear, and then it will gradually decrease until that constrained windiness leaves its place;"
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	"And cauterize the place; but if you do not see it with your own eyes,"
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	"then you can treat it with remedies that disperse winds, such as fetid pills and pills of saffron, among others."
Des saiettes	Here is the French text for "Des Saiettes":
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their likenesses and according to the places on the body where they enter.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Among them there are some that have large tips, small tips, feathered ones, and ones with heads soldered on.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And those that have two corners, and those that are long, and those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the dislocation which occurs in any limb falls according to two ways: either it occurs in the main member
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	like the brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it occurs in any of these members, then the signs of death, which I will tell you about later, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	Therefore, you must beware of removing this splint, for death comes afterwards in many ways;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And if this bad sign does not appear and the splint is not deep, then remove it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	The sign of a cerebral dislocation is when the splint falls there and pierces the bone, and the facial fascia above the brain tears
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	and when there is darkness and dizziness and heaviness and redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and mixing of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps there is without fever from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps speech and voice are lost;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And from the wound comes moist white foam like pigeons' droppings, and at once a bruise of flesh appears;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then beware of treatment, and remove the splint if it is not already embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs that the splinter has fallen on the heart are that it is near the left nipple and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the splinter moves like a chicken's, and black blood comes out, and coldness and cold sweat come on, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know for certain that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a splinter that has lodged in the lung is when without any foam coming from the wound, phlegm rises up to the throat, and the patient changes color, sighs loudly, and seeks cool air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the splinter falls into the lining of the lung, it is near the ribs; and great coughing and great pain and sighing occur; and all the members from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the splinter falls into the stomach, perhaps some undigested food will come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the splinter falls into the belly and no wind comes out through the intestines, then there is no hope for a cure or for removal of the splinter.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the splinter falls into the bladder and urine comes out and there is a fever, and the patient feels great pain, know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members such as the face and neck and throat and shoulders and arms and back and thighs and legs and similar limbs are spared according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the splinter is in a nerve or an artery and it is not venomous, as happened to me once which I will tell you about so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man that a splinter fell into his eyelid at the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it and removed it from underneath the ear's fat without any injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And once I pulled out a splinter that had fallen into the fatty tissue of the eye under the membrane:
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the splinter was embedded, and I could only grasp its tip towards the wood;
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	"An arrow as large as a Turkish bow, all of one feather, light, without ears; the wound was clean, and no bad accident befell him."
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	"And he drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, which was Arab in origin with feathers:"
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	"I pulled out the barbs, and carefully extracted it until I removed the arrow; the Christian was unharmed."
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	"And an arrow had been shot into the belly of one man, whom I believed would die;"
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	"and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change."
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	"I cut the arrow and extracted it, then pulled it out gently; there was no bad outcome."
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	"And if you see a man into whom an arrow has fallen on his back, and the wound is closed;"
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	"and the arrow remains inside him, yet his natural condition does not change,"
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	"he finds no harm in any of his natural works."
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	"And you see another man into whom an arrow falls on his face, and the wound is closed;"
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	"and remains thus without suffering great pain; and many others like him."
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	"And I removed an arrow from the eye of one of the king's nobles,"
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	"which was slightly inclined towards the right side; and the arrow was completely buried"
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	"I was called to care for him after it had been three days since the arrow fell. I found the wound very narrow."
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	"I tried to grasp it with great care and delicacy, yet could not feel it at all;"
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	"and he felt pain and discomfort beneath his right ear."
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	"I thought that it was the tip of the arrow,"
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	"I applied to the wound a plaster made from atractive and digestive ingredients, so that the area would not swell;"
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	"and then I saw the tip of the arrow."
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	"I applied the plaster for eight days, and the wound closed up again; yet the sick man remained ill for a long time,"
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	"until he felt the arrow inside his eye for one day; and he told me this."
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	"I applied a corrosive ointment to the wound for many days until it reopened;"
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	"and I probed it and felt the head of the arrow lodged there."
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	"then with this same ointment I widened the wound until the head of the arrow became clearly visible;"
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	"and it took nearly four months,"
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	"and then I widened the wound so much that I inserted forceps into it; yet I could not pull out the arrow."
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	"So then I did not cease to use finesse and ingenuity in devising ways with tools until, one day, with well-made forceps I grasped it."
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	"as will be described at the end of this chapter; thus I pulled out the arrow and healed the wound."
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	"And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot regenerate:"
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	"So I healed it and the wound closed up, and the sick man was entirely cured."
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	"Now I have told you about the extraction of some arrows,"
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	"So that you may rely on what I have not mentioned, for books cannot cover everything."
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	"But wise masters compare even small details and things which are present or lacking;"
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	"they find new works and nine tools for the extraction of foreign bodies which occur in this art."
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	"I say that arrows enter the limbs into which they are driven in only two ways:"
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	"either through the point of entry or through another part;"
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	"And that which is driven in forcefully through the same opening whence it entered, this is an arrow entering into flesh wounds, and sometimes they do not emerge again."
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	"And if it does not come out immediately, leave it there until the flesh has rotted around it, and then remove the exit;"
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	"And also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it there for a few days and moisten it each day;"
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	"and then it will come out; if not, carefully bore around it with a fine drill until the area is widened, and then pull it out."
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	"And if the arrowhead is stuck in the bone of the skull and extends as far as one of the ventricles of the brain,"
