et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	"do not pull it out at all, but leave it there until it becomes equalized after a few days;"
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	"for if the arrowhead comes close to this point, it is fatal."
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	"And if the arrowhead is stuck only in the bone and does not come near the aforesaid point,"
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	"and the sick man remains free of bad symptoms for a few days, then try to pull it out."
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if it is deeply stuck and cannot come out easily, then apply poultices around it as I have told you; then treat the area until it heals."
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	"And if the arrowhead is lodged in an internal organ where it cannot be seen, search for it everywhere;"
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	"and if you find it, pull it out with some suitable tool."
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	"And if you cannot reach it because of the narrowness of the wound or the depth of the arrowhead,"
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	"then widen the wound until it is large enough;"
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	"and pull out the arrowhead if you can; and if there are barbs on it that cause it to adhere,"
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	"then remove the flesh that is stuck in its two barbs, as much as you can;"
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	"and then break off or bend back the barbs of the arrowhead so that you can pull it out."
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	"And be careful not to break the shaft of the arrow, for otherwise pulling it out would cause more pain."
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	"And if you cannot pull it out all at once, leave it until the flesh around has rotted away, and then pull it out; for extraction will be easier."
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	"And if the flow of blood opposes you, apply what we have said about treatment in its chapter;"
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	"and beware of cutting into nerves and veins; use skill so that you can pull out the arrowhead without danger."
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	"Sooner or later, firmly or gently; place the sick man according to the position he was in when the arrow struck him;"
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	"for this is the greatest help that can be given, and if you cannot do so, place him according to what his symptoms indicate."
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	"The arrowhead which comes out on the other side, or where something of it is visible, or where the skin is swollen around it so that one can see or feel it externally:"
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	"then cut there until forceps can reach it, and then pull it out; if it comes out easily."
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	"And if it is held in the bone, rotate your hand around until it enters the bone and widen the bone, then pull it out."
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	"And if it cannot come out, leave it again and then resume extraction until it comes out completely;"
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	"and if the shaft of the arrowhead is still there, remove it with the entire shaft."
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	"And if the shaft has fallen off and you wish to apply a poultice, then use a hairy tool;"
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	"So that the point of the arrowhead enters into the hairs of the tool; then apply the poultice."
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	"And if the arrowhead is stuck in hair, insert an instrument with a pointed end among the hairs to facilitate extraction;"
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrowhead has touched, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	"And if the arrow falls into the thigh or the belly or the bladder or the side, and it is close by, you can try to push against it."
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	"And beware of pushing into the wound and the nerve, then extract [the arrow], and then stitch up the wound if necessary."
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	"and treat it until it is healed."
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	"The shape of the tweezers used to remove arrows resembles a bird's beak, and here is the illustration:"
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	"And there are many kinds [of tweezers]: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow."
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	"The shape of the arrow extractor is also like the feather of a bird,"
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	"to put on the tip of the arrow, as this is the shape:"
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	"The shape of the tweezers for grasping and pulling out is like this:"
des voinnes dou cors communes	"for common wounds of the body,"
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	"Of those from which one recovers, there are thirty-one, of which sixteen are on the head."
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	"That is to say: two blows that are behind the ears, called 'dous herbech' in old French;"
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	"and the two arteries that are visible in the two temples."
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	"and two veins in the inner corners of the two eyes, called 'aspirites'."
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	"and the vein that is on the forehead; and the wound that is on the back of the neck;"
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	"and the two jugular veins that are in the neck;"
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	"and the two veins that are above the mouth on the lips, which are called 'augeherich'."
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	"And two veins that are under the tongue."
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	"The wounds from which one commonly recovers are five in each arm:"
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	"The first is the cephalic vein, and it is on the right side, and lay people call it 'the vein of the head'."
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	"And the second is called 'faste', and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins,"
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	"and laypeople call it 'the vein of the heart'; and the basilic one is on the left side,"
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	"And they call it in common language 'vein of the belly', and it is on the bladder."
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	"And this is the one that opens visibly onto the pouch."
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	" And the savior vein is the vein that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches;"
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	"And in the leg and foot there are three veins: one of which is located under the curve of the pouch of the left side,"
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	"and the second is behind the ankle on the right side; and the vein called 'the nest', which is located in the heel of the other side;"
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	"And in the other leg there are three veins below them."
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	"The purging of veins that appear behind the ears helps with catarrh and headache."
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	"And the qualities of purging are such that you should raise the head of the patient,"
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	"and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth, then make the patient cough by having them turn their neck to one side."
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	"until the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent areas of the head:"
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	"So place your fingers there and where you feel the pulse under your finger, then squeeze gently;"
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	"then take the lancet, insert it underneath the vein until it reaches the bone, then lift your hand up along the entire length of the vein upstream,"
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	"And cut through the skin and the vein with two fingers held horizontally, and let blood flow out until you see it."
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	"then compress and tie off the vein until it is emptied;"
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	"And I have already spoken about the incision and cautery in the first book."
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	"The purging of the two arteries that are located on either side of the temples helps with headaches."
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	"and helps with eye pain, and watery eyes caused by grief in the heart;"
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	"And the qualities of purging are such that I tell you,"
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	"and it is necessary for the patient to strain their neck so that both veins appear clearly;"
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	"and feel the pulse beneath your finger, then gently squeeze."
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	"then lift the skin up along the vein using your right index finger and insert the lancet underneath;"
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	"And then lift the vein upward and cut it, just like you did with the other two veins, and let blood flow according to your needs;"
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	"then release the patient, place your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton;"
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	"And then tie it firmly and leave it until it is emptied of blood; and I have already spoken about their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book."
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	"The purging of the frontal vein is just as useful for treating old facial diseases, headaches and redness."
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	"And its qualities are such that the patient should strain their neck by twisting it so that the vein appears;"
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	"then take the instrument called 'the borer', which is shaped like this:"
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	"And place the point on the vein and press down with your hand or something else, and let blood flow out according to the amount you desire;"
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	"then release the patient's neck and tie off the vein until it is emptied of blood, using a wide flame."
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	"However, make sure the flame is not too large; and cut across the vein, for the bone is close by, and sometimes the flame may break if it is too thin."
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	"The purging of the two veins located on either side of the nose helps with nosebleeds, tinea capitis, redness, and eye inflammation, and facial diseases."
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	"And its qualities are such that the patient should strain their neck by twisting it in any direction, just like before;"
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	"then make the cut across the vein with a slightly long and wide flame, for there is little flesh present."
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	"And if the flame is too thin it may break; then let blood flow until you have enough, and then apply cotton and tie it firmly."
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	"The purging of the nasal vein is useful for treating colds, feverish insanity, and facial diseases,"
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	"especially for treating headaches and redness that appear on the face, especially when they are chronic;"
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	"And its qualities are such that the patient should strain their neck, then pinch their nose with your left hand,"
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	"and take a thin, long flame and insert it into the space between the two nostrils;"
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	"for the vein does not appear well there, and blood will begin to flow now."
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	"And do not go in too deep, and let blood flow according to your needs, then tie it off for one night, for it is quickly restored;"
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	"This is the shape of the flame:"
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	"The purging of the two glands helps with the swelling of the glands, and the onset of glandular fever, and many diseases, including eczema, skin erosion, and herpetic sores."
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	"And its qualities are such that the patient should strain their neck beneath either side, as we have said;"
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	"and let the master stand on top of the patient's head, and let the patient lie on one elbow;"
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	"then cut the vein along its length slightly widely, then let blood flow moderately, or until enough is obtained;"
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	"then repeat on the other side, then release the ligature and gently squeeze both veins;"
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	"so that the patient does not strangle, and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed."
De la sainie des leivres	Of bloodletting from the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting of the veins above the lips helps with colds in the mouth, gum decay, cracked lips, and the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	"And its qualities are such that you should make the patient sit before you, and strain their neck as I have said;"
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	"then turn the lip and look for the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left;"
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	"And recognize them by their dark color, and by the small black veins around them;"
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	"then cut both of them, but if you do not know how to do it or are uncertain,"
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	"then cut the largest one on each side, and likewise cut both of the veins above and below, for it is the same method."
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of bloodletting under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bloodletting of the veins under the tongue helps after the bloodletting from the head, and it is used for swelling in the throat, diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth."
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	"And its qualities are such that the patient should sit between your hands facing the sun, raise their tongue, and look for a black vein on each side underneath;"
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	"then cut both of them, but do not go in too deep, for the arteries are located underneath."
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm that are commonly bled are let according to two methods:"
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	"either with one wide, round flame, or with an olive-shaped thin flame like a cutting edge, and it is called 'anesil';"
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	"And they are wide and thin according to the size and swelling of the veins."
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the round flame is very well-known, and it is wide as you see:"
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	"And one must use for opening the hairy veins filled with thick visible blood, which contain thick and turbid blood;"
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	"and it is the form of the olive-shaped flame:"
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	"And it is more subtly pointed and is for cauterizing the subtle veins where there is subtle citrine blood."
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	"The cautery of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are below the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen;"
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	"And it behooves the cauterizer to cauterize skillfully and to beware of the artery that is underneath."
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	"And if he cuts the artery, and blood begins to flow, then it behooves him to cauterize it immediately as I have said;"
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	"And the flame must not be sharp, but cutting like a knife."
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	"If the basilica vein does not open manifestly, then it behooves you to extract it and change another;"
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	"or wherever you want any branch of it, or you cauterize in place of it the vein that is in the arm; it opens manifestly."
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	"And cut it with a knife-shaped flame as we have said."
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	"And if you wish to know the place of cauterization, then it behooves you beforehand to extract the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse;"
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	"then mark the place with ink and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with a knife-shaped flame."
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	"And beware that you do not strike the artery when you see the place distended, for it is of the artery; avoid it therefore."
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	"And if you see something like urine coming out above, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is arterial blood:"
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	"then quickly place your thumb upon it and remove it if the bleeding stops, for this happens many times."
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	"If you bind the arm thus, leave it like that and do not move the limb of the sick person; let him be quiet in fear, and do not move it until he is healed."
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	"And if the blood does not stop and it is flowing freely, and there is no physician present, then cut the artery if it opens, for its source draws back; and cauterize the blood."
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	"And take a fig-wood bark, split it open, take one half of it and bind it firmly until the next day;"
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	"If the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then cauterize it with powders that stop bleeding as we have said."
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	"And cauterization should not be taken lightly in many conditions because of the smallness of the wound and the power of the ligature on the arm."
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	"The cauterization of the vein in the middle aids so that it draws blood from above the head and from below the body,"
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	"because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic veins as we have said;"
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	"And the surgeon must beware of the nerve that is underneath, and if it is not too deep, he will find the nerve,"
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	"and if it swells and the saint suffers harm, then perhaps he cannot heal;"
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	"And this nerve opens frequently and if it does not open in some men because of its subtlety, then you must cauterize it with the knife-shaped flame; and avoid the nerve as much as possible."
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	"And if there is a vein between the two nerves, split it lengthwise."
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	"The cauterization of the cephalic vein aids so that it draws blood from the head and helps also in other ways;"
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	"And it is necessary to cauterize in a puncturing manner with the olive-shaped flame or the myrtle-shaped flame, for this is the safest of all veins since there are neither nerve nor artery beneath it."
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	"Nevertheless, one must seek out the easiest place and not worry if one fails the first time; one should begin again;"
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	"And sometimes the places swell in some men when one fails the first time, but it does no harm."
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	"The quality of cauterization depends on your skill."
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	"The first thing you must know about cauterization is that it is not introduced except for the sake of preserving health,"
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	"and to avoid future illnesses;"
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	"And let cauterization be done in one of the three veins that are on the forearm: namely, the cephalic, the basilic, or the median cubital."
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	"And one should cauterize at the beginning of Lent and in autumn and winter after meals when the sign of repletion appears;"
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	"And one should cauterize on the first or third day, after two or three hours from noon."
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	"Cauterization that is administered for illnesses has no fixed time, but rather whenever there is need on a certain day or night, at all hours and at all times;"
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	"And one should not cauterize children until they are fourteen years old, nor women during pregnancy except from the fourth month until the seventh."
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	"Nor should one cauterize the elderly who have passed sixty years of age."
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	"And when anyone wants to be cauterized, in whatever manner it may be, they must cleanse the bowels with a light enema,"
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	"especially if there is much retained feces so that the veins do not draw out the impurities from the bowels which could harm the principal members;"
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	"nor should one cauterize anyone who is too salty from eating meat or who is drunk, until they sober up, nor anyone with dropsy;"
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	"And one should beware of cauterizing after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent urination in women, hard labor, sleeplessness, fasting, or any weakness of body, whether caused by an injury or by some other cause."
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	"Then refine the humors if the blood is thick, through diet and drink and medicine, if you have the ability;"
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	"then take a bath, if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood;"
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	"and cauterize the vein on the arm around the third hour, as we have said;"
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	"And guard yourself that day from hard labor, overeating, lust, and similar things;"
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	"and be calm and happy, and let the cauterizer be taller than the person being cauterized, and rub the arm two or three times;"
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	"then remove the ligature from the middle because if it is too tight or loose, then the blood cannot flow properly;"
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	"And then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt;"
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	"then let the cauterizer wet the flame with a little old oil, and then place his thumb of his left hand on that vein below the place where he intends to cauterize;"
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	"So that the vein does not slip or move during the cautery."
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	"Because there are veins that flee like ropes during cauterization, and some are so full of windiness,"
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	"That when one puts the flame upon them, they retreat from the flame and cannot open the vein, and this is how it is with some people;"
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	"And if he opens the vein, then the wound will be too narrow, so that the cauterizer must be skilled in these matters."
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	"And if the vein opens on the first attempt, that is good. But if not, then begin again a little below or above that place immediately, if the area is not swollen;"
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	"And if the place is swollen, and the patient fears it, let him wait one or two days, without binding the arm:"
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	"Perhaps an abscess will appear; do not enter a bath, then resume treatment if he wishes."
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	"And if the hole is small, or the skin cuts finely and you doubt that there might not be as much blood coming out as you see, then apply fire to that same hole directly."
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	"And work hastily, before the place becomes swollen; for this happens often when the wound is small."
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	"If you see the place swollen, do not resume treatment and apply a little oil mixed with honey; for it lightens the body of blood and is moisturizing in this place."
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	"And thus apply the mixture of oil and honey at each treatment that you give to veins, so as to stop the flow of blood."
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	"And this same mixture also works well for dropsy and bowel obstructions when applied to the place; for it thins the blood and disperses it when it is too thick."
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	"And if there appears a large abscess which happens often, especially when the vein is not treated but at that single time when the wound was small,"
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	"then be quick and apply to the place a sponge moistened in warm water mixed with salt, and keep it on for an hour."
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	"And you should do this after the bleeding from the vein has ceased; and if there remains on the place some blackness or greenness for several days afterwards, it will not harm."
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	"And if you see that it is necessary to apply something made of aloe or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, mastich, or similar substance."
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	"And often there occurs an abscess and appearance during the treatment of the basilica (the great vein); therefore place your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft under pressure from your hand, then this is a bad sign."
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Therefore be careful not to apply any of the things we have mentioned, for it might happen that it will cut into the artery without notice; but rather make a dry poultice to harden the place and then treat it with another treatment until it is healed."
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	"And draw from each according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood."
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	"For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if it appears thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool."
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	"And it is necessary for those who are full and fat and have need of bloodletting to make the cut larger and to use a wide blade."
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	"And for those who are weak, do the opposite; they should be bled little and often, and they should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking."
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	"And this manner of bleeding saves from loss of blood and from injury to the nerves, and is better than a long or wide cut."
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	"And for those whose body fails from bleeding, it is necessary to give them bread moistened in pomegranate juice; if they are heated, let them bleed three or four times."
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	"And if they are of cold temperament, let them eat before bleeding bread moistened in thick syrup or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a fragrant syrup."
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	"And if they faint during bleeding, after the flow of much blood, it is necessary that they inhale broth of meat and a fragrant, subtle syrup."
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	"and use the other things we have mentioned in the section on syncope for evacuating veins."
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	"And if he wishes to empty one arm and bleed elsewhere another time, when he is weakened by much bleeding, it is necessary that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his continued strength."
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	"And whoever wishes to empty one arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong body, should bleed again 24 hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour."
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	"And whoever wishes to bleed elsewhere should bleed on the second or third day."
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	"For there is much blood in the body which is already heated and causes fever; therefore it is necessary to draw a large quantity of blood and widen the opening so that it flows easily."
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	"Then when you have prepared all the conditions for bleeding and placed your hand on the pulse as it bleeds, make sure that the mouth does not come into contact with the opening."
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	"And this happens very often when the bloodletter is negligent."
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	"And it should not be done when you wish to release the arm and cause blood to flow out a second time, for then the opening is closed, you should press strongly upon it."
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	"nor if he is curved, let him extend his arm quickly, for this would be harmful."
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	"But let it flow until it bleeds the second time; or you may prick with the tip of the blade so that the frozen blood which blocks the vein opening flows out."
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	"And place a little bit of fresh moss in water and press upon it lightly."
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	"And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not compress it until the swelling has subsided."
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	"And if there is need to draw blood a second time, then bleed in the same vein or in another vein or in the other arm."
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	"The veins of the arm are bled instead of the cephalic vein because they are composed [of many small veins]."
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	"And the manner of bleeding is that the patient places his hand in warm water until the veins appear red;"
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	"then let it be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, and then bleed across, not wide or long."
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	"And let the opening be wide and bleed close to the joint of the hand; if blood cannot flow out, then place the hand back in warm water and allow the blood to flow into the water until you have enough."
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	"And if it is summer, do not place the hand back in warm water, for this is done more often in winter than in summer."
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	"And bleeding from this vein is safer than from all others because there are neither arteries nor nerves there."
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	"Bleeding of the basilica vein of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it should be done:"
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand steady, and immerse it in hot water until the vein becomes visible.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	If the vein is swollen and if you bind all around, then there will be no injury;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	"And do not cut too deep for beneath all flesh lie nerves."
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	"And then immerse the hand in warm water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot flow out."
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	"And once you have removed as much blood as necessary, then place oil and lint on it to seal it quickly, and do the same for each wound."
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	"The urine from the left hand is good for treating mousse disease, and do everything as I have told you regarding the right hand."
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	"Sphenoid bone urine is beneficial for all diseases that occur beneath the body."
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Such as marrow disease, retention of flowers (possibly referring to menstrual disorders), and diseases of the reins, thighs, and old legs, as well as similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	"And its urine's property is such that patients can soak their feet in warm water and rub the wound until it becomes soft."
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	"Then place their foot on the knee; the wound is at the ankle, and many veins run from there to the foot;"
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Therefore, treat it where the largest vein or at the ankle.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	"And if you treat it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath it, and cut across just as when cutting meat; let the blade be sterile."
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	"And if blood cannot flow out, then immerse the foot in water and allow the vein to empty well."
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	"If the cauterization does not succeed on the first try, then begin again a little higher up because the area is already burnt;"
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	"do not hesitate to cut the nerve, as we have said, and do the same for the other sphenoid bone on the other foot equally."
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	"The scar of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle, and its urine is beneficial for treating hip pain when it's due to hot blood."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	"And its property is such that the patient enters a bath and strains four fingers while twisting over the ankle;"
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	"because otherwise the vein will not open, and if it opens, cauterize it in every way that you can, including across it."
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	"And it's better for you to cut it because the scar is smooth, and it's very responsive to many people."
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	"If you cannot find it, then cauterize any vein that opens on the back of the foot and towards the little toe, but beware of nerves;"
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	"And do so until you see blood flow, then untie the bandage, put cotton on it and bind it again; now it is cauterized."
Des sainies de ventouse	Regarding the treatment of varicose veins
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made from horn, glass, or earthenware and there are two ways of applying them: either by pricking and attracting blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this application without pricking is done in two ways: either with fire or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And the application that involves pricking and blood extraction is performed on fourteen parts of the body;
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	namely, one is at the top of the head, another in the neck;"
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on either side of the neck; and the one under the chin;"
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and those on both shoulders, and that above the elbows;"
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and those on both arms, and those on both legs;"
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and those at the ankles; and cupping does not draw blood except from small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh."
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And therefore it does not weaken anyone, unlike cauterizing veins;"
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered with or without fire in any disease that comes frompletion until the whole body is emptied."
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it becomes necessary to apply cupping because of illness or custom, we will administer it at each hour from the beginning to the end of the month, and during every season;"
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need cupping, have heavy heads;"
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and others findpletion and redness in their face, head, neck, and darkness before the eyes;"
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, have an enlarged tongue, and spit blood;"
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And there are those who dream and see things like blood, wounds, death, and similar things."
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during the month of May, we order cupping to be performed after three hours of the day."
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The cautery for the temple helps with headaches that occur in certain people, and it should not be performed after evacuating the entire body;"
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this cupping is a substitute for the cautery of the temporal vein;"
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and those who have cold constitutions or phlegm should not use it, as it causes them great harm;"
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore old men and those with cold conditions in the head should not use it."
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often cauterize themselves become forgetful, so it is necessary to place the cupping jar a little further down to avoid forgetfulness."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Cupping on the neck is equivalent to cauterizing the head and the basilica veins, and it is particularly useful for chest congestion;"
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for coughs, asthma, andpletion;"
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	But it should not be placed too firmly, as otherwise it could cause forgetfulness or harm the stomach or heart."
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	Cupping on both sides of the neck is beneficial for headaches, eyestrain, migraines, chest congestion, and toothache;"
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is a substitute for cauterizing the basilica veins. Make sure to tell the cauterizer not to cut the artery or cause excessive bleeding."
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Cupping under the chin is beneficial for mouth diseases, gingivitis, and similar conditions in the mouth, and it is a substitute for cauterizing both lips;"
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping on the shoulders is beneficial for illnesses caused by heat andpletion."
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	Cupping on the elbows is as effective as cauterizing three veins in the arm;"
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it draws blood from these large veins;"
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and tell the cauterizer not to pry too deeply, as this area lacks flesh and has nerves and arteries underneath."
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping jar placed on the buttocks is beneficial for hemorrhoids and lower abdominal diseases. The jar should be large and made of earthenware to draw well without breaking and causing large wounds."
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping on the legs draws blood from all over the body and is particularly beneficial for treating chronic back pain, sciatica, bladder problems, and gout. It serves as a substitute for cauterizing both sophenes veins and ankles, but prolonged use can weaken the body and cause paleness in various conditions."
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	To apply the cupping jar, you should first place it empty on the skin and suck temperately until the skin turns red and inflamed. Then quickly place the jar and move it evenly without stopping until you see the skin turn red with blood. After that, remove the jars, being careful about the condition of the person's body, as some have thin skin and fair pores; in such cases, it is best to cauterize only once, making wide and somewhat deep wounds, and sucking gently."
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	"And if the blood is thick, then one must strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood."
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	"And if the blood is very dense, then one must strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out just a little blood drop by drop, then once will suffice."
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	"And if we wish for much blood, let us strike often; and if the blood is dense, then strike deeply, ensuring that the heart is pierced suddenly,"
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	"And those with thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, must anoint the places for the cups with oil that is aperient and dissolving:"
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is inflamed, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or gourd seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in a cold state, use mustard oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, then take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	If one has tender flesh and wide pores, no oil should be applied there.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But after the application of vapor, one should wash it with rosewater, or cold water, or cranberry juice, or gourd juice, or porcelain juice, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who are very moist should rise using myrtle water, sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large swellings should rise with old wine, or buckthorn water, or decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	And one should not apply cupping before or during the bath, but rather afterwards for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And they should be careful to warm themselves both when applying the cups and when being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	Beware those who are being treated have a choleric complexion, and whose skin is too dry and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	"If it is necessary for them to take cold things, such as pomegranates and endive, lettuce, and similar things."
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink chicory, roasted pork meat, moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion should take honey syrup and moderate perfumed wine that is between old and new, and eat chicken and young birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day when he goes to vomit, he should drink more than he eats
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and sometimes it is necessary to give certain people three times the amount of treacle or muscatel before vomiting, or afterwards, to strengthen the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Let the breath be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The cups that are placed without striking are those placed on the liver, spleen, kidneys and ankles, stomach, belly, loins, buttocks and thighs, for these members do not suffer being struck upon.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and this is only done to draw blood from member to member
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	just as we place cups on the breasts when there is a damp heat, to remove viscosity from the member, so we place cups on the stomach and belly to reduce the member
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and relieves pain when there is congestion or stone, sometimes removing the congestion or shifting the stone from its place through its attractive virtue
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	Thus it also does when placed on the liver and spleen where retention of wind exists
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cups are administered empty merely to suck, sometimes they are administered together with fire, and at other times filled with hot water
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	just as in cases of pleurisy, and so that one fills the cup with warm water alone, or water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of administering the cupping glass with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and on the side around the middle there should be one small hole, like that for inserting a needle,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	"Whether made of brass, soften it first so it does not burn the patient when placing it on the limb;"
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	"And let there be in the middle a transverse rod of brass or iron to hold a candle."
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	"[Let them have] both large and small ones, according to the diseases and the size of those who wear them."
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	"For the cupping glasses of children are different from those of the elderly, and those for the thin are different from those for the fat."
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	"And so one should place this cupping glass onto the limb:"
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	"Light the candle made of wax or linseed oil, and insert it into the cupping glass through the transverse rod that is inside the cupping glass,"
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	"So that the flame reaches the bottom of the cupping glass without burning the patient;"
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	"And then place it onto the limb, ensuring that it is over the hole we mentioned earlier so that steam can be released when desired and the cupping glass removed."
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	"And then apply the liniment as before, repeating this process frequently if needed."
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	"In the case of the cupping glass used for pleurisy or acute diseases, there is no transverse rod nor hole. It is only filled with water when it is full, and it is placed onto the limb alone."
et c’est li forme:	"This is its shape:"
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	"Sanguis cupping glasses are used only in places where regular cupping glasses cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar locations."
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	"And in areas of flesh devoid of hair, such as the scalp, eyebrows, and other similar locations;"
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	"The qualities of using sanguis cupping glasses are that when you find them without any apparent holes or damage, use them;"
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	"And place them in warm water for a while until they become soft and have nothing inside them;"
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	"Then clean the cupping glass and sanguis cupping glass, rub the limb until it becomes red, and place the sanguis cupping glasses onto it;"
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	"And when they become full and begin to droop, if it is a location where a regular cupping glass can be placed, do so, as this is very beneficial."
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	"If not, then lift the limb gently and then rinse it with warm water, and finally squeeze it out;"
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	"If the limb is too dry after removing the sanguis cupping glasses, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and place it over the area to dilate the blood vessels;"
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	"And if there is too much bleeding, apply powdered vitriol or salt and similar substances to stop the bleeding;"
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	"Or you can place half a handful of peeled fava beans onto the area and leave them until they warm up against the skin, which will now stop the bleeding;"
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	"And if you need to use more sanguis cupping glasses, take additional ones."
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	"And if the sanguis cupping glasses will not adhere, rub the area with fresh blood or prick it with a needle until blood flows out;"
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	"Then place them onto the area and as soon as they sense the blood, they will adhere."
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	"And when you see that they are full and dripping, apply a little powder made of ground aloe and salt or ashes to make them droop."
Ci comence li livre des brisures	"Here begins the book of fractures"
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a remedy for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish physicians neglect this chapter, having neither seen any of the ancient books nor read a letter about it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And because of this, knowledge in our land is strange, for I never found anyone good with this.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	"And I know nothing about it except through the knowledge of old books which I have studied so much that I have written about this science, and through experience, and through the practice of my life."
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	"I have described for you in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the shapes of the instruments that are arranged, as I have done in these two chapters before."
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of words and chapters where the wise puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are skilled know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	"I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain occurs to anyone, it is necessary for you to hasten to heal the sick on both sides, if possible, except in cases of weakness of body, childhood, or old age;"
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	"unless the time is very hot or too cold; and eat cold foods, that is to say cold drinks, and flesh of fowl and hare, and do not drink wine nor eat fatty meats, nor fill yourself too full with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about a hot aposteme, nor expansion of matter in the limb; then bring back the sick person to their previous regimen that they had used."
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that you feed the sick person with foods that promote growth and viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, eggs, fish, milk, wine, and similar things."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For with this nourishment muscles are rebuilt more quickly and the fracture heals sooner."
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	"And know that the bones of the elderly and those who are decrepit do not heal well nor fuse according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children;"
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	"but take care and attach a splint made of one large beam to the broken bone, joining it together so that it strengthens as it was before; do not remove the device until the work is complete, and for this reason they must be nourished with fatty meats, as we have said."
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that fractures are diverse in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the arm or the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways that fractures can occur."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"For there are fractures that go to the bone and others that do not affect the bone, such as cutting off the tip of a quill for writing."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And there is fracture with wound, and fracture with just a small crack."
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	"And each type of fracture has its own method and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory comes into place;"
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	"and a fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the site is twisted and clearly visible through deficiency, and it sounds hollow when pressed with the hand;"
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	"and when there is no twist nor sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture."
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	"But it may still have twisting, cracking, or a small fracture."
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move the limb by hand, but apply the medicines that are mentioned below and then gently immobilize it."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	"And know that fractures which affect the bone and consist of two disjointed parts must be set back in place evenly before any inflammation occurs;"
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	"and if inflammation has already occurred, leave it alone for a few days until the inflammation is reduced;"
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	"then set it back in place gently and smoothly, and know that restoring this fracture is easier than restoring those with broken pieces. Then immobilize it as needed."
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	"And if the bone has broken into pieces, then grasp it with two hands if it is an arm or leg, or use one hand for smaller limbs, or use two cords or one cord and your hand;"
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	"and place the limb according to its natural shape so that when the broken pieces are aligned, use all means to attach them in their proper places without causing injury or pain to the patient;"
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	"And join the two ends of the bones together with the best possible alignment."
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	"And you can tell by feeling if it is not properly aligned: straighten it gently and do not immobilize it too tightly or apply pressure as some people do to cause inflammation and contractions in the limb, as we have said many times."
