It is necessary that you wrap a hard doubled bandage around the break, removing any excess material, then turn the leg so that the heel is at the root of the thighbone, and insert a long thread between the thigh and calf near the knee below, with both ends coming out on top; then wrap the bandage up the leg and thigh again, placing wedges over the break and one wedge on the shin bone, then fill the space between the leg and thigh with soft cloth to ensure equal tension, then begin tying firmly with three or four turns above the break, decreasing the tension as you move farther from the break; then tie the two ends of the thread that were inserted between the leg and thigh to the three wedges placed on top, then return to the bottom end of the thread until you reach the foot, pulling tightly so it doesn’t move from its place, then leave it like this until no infection or inflammation occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if an infection occurs, untie it and treat what has occurred, as we have said many times before; and if there are pieces of bone sticking out, they should be removed if possible; and if not, then the space should be opened up and pus drained; and the treatment should continue as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thighbone may break in such a way that wedges are not used, as in the case of the arm; nevertheless, with this treatment there is no impairment to the patient's mobility.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thighbone takes about one month to heal, give or take a few days depending on individual constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Regarding the kneecap
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that the kneecap rarely breaks but often dislocates. If it does break, it is usually just a fissure or hole, which happens with and without pain, although this can be well felt.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is to place what was dislocated back in its proper position as best as possible, then apply splints and possibly a round wedge if needed, tying it securely. Then follow all the instructions given for other fractures regarding infection, heat, etc., applying whatever remedies are necessary until healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Regarding bone fractures of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that the leg has two bones called "fibula" and "tibia," with the same types of fractures occurring as in the arm. Therefore, treatment is also the same, using the same techniques for reduction and splinting.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken at once, turn the leg in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bone is broken, so turn [it] forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, so there will be great pain, and it can be seen clearly; and turn [it] downward. Therefore prepare an extension, and place [it] evenly, and bind the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly, and there are many pieces, then make the extension smaller and lighter; and adjust according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, then take two strips of wood smoothed that wrap around the leg on either side, and are the length of the leg from the knee downwards; then wind around them twice with a bandage above and below, and tie them in the middle likewise, and at this tying the leg will not be able to bend to the right or left, and so it is well. And some people provide one splint made of wood that is the length of the leg, and place the leg upon it to prevent movement, and this is properly done at the site of the fracture where there is a wound; and move the leg each day to see if there is any hot swelling or other accident; so care must be taken until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	About the fracture of bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	In the ankle there is no fracture, but sometimes a bone in the foot is broken and in two pieces, and there occurs only quassure in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bone in the foot, and you see these bones protruding one over the other, then put your foot on the ground like someone who wants to walk, and then place your foot upon his where the bones are raised, and press down until they return to their places; then put splints and bandages on it, and place under the instep of the foot a small table with two holes filled with plaster, and strap it firmly against the foot forwardly, and then wrap cloths around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, then untie the bandage, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the toes broken, then restore them as we have said for the toes of the hand; then place on the broken toe a splint according to its length, and let it be a little wider, then place under the foot that table which I mentioned, and strap it firmly against the foot forwards; and if there are two or three, or more, toes broken, then place on each toe a splint according to their quantity, wrapped in one linen cloth, and strap the table under the foot; and let them be standing upon the top of the table so that they touch well the sole of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have mentioned for other fractures, and take care of each accident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	About the fracture of the bone of the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the thumb is broken in a woman, then make her sit upright, then incline her towards the back and let her be held by someone behind her; then fill the thumb with cotton, and put in it as big as one walnut; then raise the woman up little by little, and now the cotton will come to the entrance of the thumb, and the bone will return with the walnut; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do so for about seven days: then the fracture will be restored. And if you see, take a bladder of a sheep, and tie a tube at the opening, and put the whole bladder inside the thumb; then blow into the tube strongly until the bladder is inflated inside: then the thumb will return to its fractured place; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the thumb of a man or woman is broken, then restore it as we have said for the bone of the heel; and these fractures are not hidden from those who put their study and use in it, and understand my book. For the fracture indicates in many ways the right way to restoration: therefore, pay attention to it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose neck and put it around the penis; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three or four days around, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	About fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	He who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or the arm or similar, must be healed now, so that the healing that we have mentioned proves it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then rinse it with vitriol, if you don't have anything else, then begin to restore the fracture in that same hour or day, if no inflammation occurs.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if inflammation occurs, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the inflammation is appeased, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring bad accidents upon it.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing above the exposed heart, then it must be put in place lightly with your hands, with slight traction.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not convenient for you to put it in place with your hands, then use this instrument which is made of iron, which has seven or eight fingers long, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the surgeon to prepare three or four, according to what he needs in each case of fracture. And let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb during your operation, and let it be pointed at the front, and thicker towards the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called a "palainche," because the curved bone must be placed on top of the exposed bone; and push it in at once until it returns, and let them be equal one against the other. And if the fracture is slight, and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, then cut off the end of the bone so that the instrument can have hold of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, then cut off with an appropriate instrument such as the chisel or saw according to your ability; then scrape what remains on the bone with sharpness and small scrapings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is put back in place and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position. Then do whatever is necessary to put it back in its proper place, then moisten one cloth in black styptic wine, and apply it properly if it is in summer; and do not put on the wound cerote or anything else with oil, for it will bring corruption and decay. Then apply bandages when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and be sure that the wound is not constrained with the fracture; and many times foolish surgeons have done this and brought death or corrosion upon the patient. And let the binding be softer and more gentle than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents will come of it, as we have said, and you find pain in its place, then one should not put on bandages; but wrap it around tightly with hard cloths, and tie them. And when after one or two days you see that the wound begins to heal, then remove what you have placed there, and put on healing ointment such as tetrafarmakon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	You must wash the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is solid and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	The limb should be placed in such a way that the wound drains easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and the wound does not heal but continues to suppurate, know that there are small bone fragments present, for which reason you should cleanse the wound with tincture and remove all these unwanted fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula appears in the place, or some other type of corruption, then you should treat it according to what is said in its chapter above. And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the hip bone or the shoulder blade, and others like them on large limbs, do not pull it out for many times the flesh follows it; let it remain until it rots; perhaps it will fall off by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	about the burns that come on top of the scab
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Many times after the fracture has healed, burns can appear on top of the scab, especially if it is near the joint, and the appearance of the limb is unpleasant; and sometimes the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, beware if the bone is fresh: have the physician administer medicines that are astringent, such as aloe, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocol, acacia, and similar others; so that you take any of these things or all together, and confit them with wine that is astringent or with egg yolk or with oil; and put them on the bone in bandages, and tie it tightly and do not untie it for many days; then remove it, and start another one again until the inflammation is gone; or you can bind it to a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs. And if the inflammation has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut off what is on top and remove the excess; or have a barber shave it until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	about the limb that is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When bone fracture is healed,
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is thus: you should make the patient eat, and stretch the body so that blood multiplies within them; the servant should give baths, and bring joy and laughter; then place poultice on the limb so that it attracts to great nourishment, and repeatedly wash it with hot water until the nourishment reaches the limb; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb twisted after recovery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone breaks openly, and the form of the limb is misshapen, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: thus do not believe the foolish who say that one must break the limb again anew, for many a foolish physician has done this in our land; and such operations are blameworthy, and great evils result, and sometimes even death. Nonetheless, if the dislocations and distortions are recent, they should be bathed with hot water or mollifying herbs cooked therein, such as fig leaves and roots, and mullein, and like substances; and make one mollifying poultice, such as well-made diacere, and take the mucilage of figs and cook it with goose grease or sesame oil, and apply the poultice thereon; or take ripe figs and grind them with coltsfoot, and like medicines that soften the union.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the dislocation is removed by continuous rubbing for a long time with moist hands. And let the limb be moved each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twistings are old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove them with iron, then one must cut down to the bone, gently with a sharp lancet; and put care and skill into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations are when a joint leaves its place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misshapen, and the sufferer feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, they should try to reduce it immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the place becomes inflamed, and perhaps it will not be set back in its proper place. Therefore one should not attempt to move it when it is inflamed: many times this brings about spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	When this occurs, nevertheless, wash the patient, then leave him until the inflammation is appeased; then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and care for each limb as it comes back into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of the dislocations from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws become dislocated upwards, and their dislocation occurs in two ways: either they are a little displaced from their places, and softened somewhat; or they are entirely dislocated, hanging towards the chest, with saliva flowing out of the mouth so that it cannot be held back, nor can the mouth be closed, and speech is impeded by the tongue.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When dislocation is slight, it returns spontaneously in most cases.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and total, then you must reset it quickly without delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in this manner that the servant holds the patient's head, and the physician places a pouch of his one hand at the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other two hands should be free to keep it even; and instructs the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician places it back until it returns to its proper place
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the dislocation is severe, especially if both jaws are dislocated together, then raise them with hot water and oil until they become slightly softened; do not force the repositioning, as we have said
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are repositioned correctly, and the patient closes his mouth without softening, then place wet cloths made with a salve of rose oil and wax on it, and bind it lightly with soft bandages
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient should sleep on his back with two pillows under his shoulders so that he does not move to the right or left and does not attempt to chew but takes only soft food until the pain is gone and the jaws are at rest
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then he may chew what he wants easily, and should not force his mouth open while eating or drinking until the jaws are fully healed and strong
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if both jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not returned to their proper positions, then fever and chills may occur, sometimes with diarrhea and occasionally vomiting of clear bile
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see these signs, know that it is a loss of life; many times the person dies within eight days
de la forcelle	of dislocation
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation cannot be dislocated from the inner side of the cheekbone nor from the breastbone; sometimes it is dislocated backward and can be felt quite well
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the reduction is done by having the patient lie on his back with arms extended, pressing firmly on the cheekbone with the palm of the hand until it returns to its place, then placing the emplastrum and binding it tightly
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the chin which is towards the face cannot be dislocated; if it can, then it should be repositioned as we have said, then place the emplastrum and bandage and bind it tightly, and tell the patient to rest until healed
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and so too is the chin of the shoulder repositioned when it has been dislocated from its place
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Chapter on the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated outward in three ways: firstly from the lower part of the socket, secondly from the side of the chest, and occasionally from above, which happens rarely
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And the shoulder does not dislocate backwards nor inward towards the nerves; often it dislocates downward toward the socket, especially in those with little flesh, for then it springs out quickly; but in those with abundant flesh, it barely springs out and scarcely returns
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there occurs a blow or fall which causes the shoulder to swell with a hot hematoma and the person believes that it is dislocated because of this
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore you must examine him closely until you are certain; then begin treatment
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known when the dislocation has occurred downward toward the socket, for there will be a noticeable difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, with clear manifestations in between
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder and beneath the socket a touch like that of an egg, and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck nor move it in any way
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and likewise if it is dislocated upward, it is not hidden but can be felt distinctly upon touching
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this manner of dislocation cannot be reduced except when it is new or if the patient is a child
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the practitioner to raise the patient's hand upwards, then place his fingers beneath the socket and forcefully raise the joint upwards into its proper place, and then lower the hand downwards
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come back as we have described within several days afterwards, then the patient must be bathed in warm water and given softening and soothing remedies to drink, such as a decoction of mallow, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and he should be treated accordingly
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then have the patient lie on his back with a piece of cloth folded into a roll placed beneath the socket, not too soft nor too hard, then place the practitioner's heel upon the cloth and gently raise the diseased shoulder while pulling the patient's hand in this way
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and another practitioner should hold the patient's head so that it does not move downwards; then the shoulder will return immediately into its proper place, and you may reduce it in this manner
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and have present one man who is larger than the patient, standing on the diseased side with his shoulder placed beneath the socket of the patient's arm and raising it upwards so that the patient hangs in the air
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another practitioner pulls the patient's arm downwards towards his belly. And if the patient is too light, have him hang with some heavy object and the dislocation will return into its proper place
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it may also be reduced in another manner thus: take a long stick and fix it firmly into the ground so that its end is as high as a man's fist and neither too thick nor too thin
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then place it beneath the patient, but let him have soft cloths underneath to prevent injury, and have him stand upon the end of the stick, then extend his arm downward forcefully on the other side and the joint will quickly return into its proper place
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it will not return by all the methods we have described, then do this treatment: take a stick two and a half feet long and four fingers wide with a rounded top to allow easy entry into the socket beneath the arm in this way
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then place soft cloths upon the top of the stick to prevent injury to the patient, then place it beneath the socket of the diseased arm; extend the patient's other arm upwards along the length of the stick and tie the elbow to the stick with a bandage, then place the forearm upon a support made from a piece of wood about half an inch thick; let the hand hang downwards on one side and allow the body to hang freely on the other side: the joint will now return into its proper place
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it has returned into its proper place, however this may have happened, then you must place a bandage of wool beneath the socket, sprinkle the whole shoulder and surrounding area with powdered mallow leaves mixed with incense and egg-white, then draw the bandage tight beneath the arm and tie the ends securely around the emplastrum; fasten the hand to its collarbone and let it remain in this position
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he fast for a few days until the member is strengthened, for it will heal more quickly; and then after five or six days he may eat again and move about, and if it remains firm without becoming softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come into it, or for another reason, then you must administer cauteries at three points, as it is set forth in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do everything, and it remains dislocated after seven days, and the shoulder cannot be raised above the arm, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never again be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations that occur toward the chest or back are caused by pushing or pulling with great force, and bandages should be applied to support them until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing there is stiffness in the limb and difficulty in movement, then let the patient exercise many times until that stiffness is alleviated and returns to its original condition.
de la dislocation dou coute	of dislocation of the neck
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the neck is easily dislocated and easily relocated; and if it has been completely dislocated, both front and back, and the dislocation cannot be reduced because it is visible and palpable in every position.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the sick neck with the healthy one, you can see it clearly because the joint is dislocated and the arm cannot be bent nor touched to the shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reduce it before inflammation comes, because if inflammation should come, reduction will be difficult and perhaps the dislocation cannot be completely reduced, especially when it is on the back; such cases are worse than others and cause greater pain, and sometimes the mouth becomes twisted.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And reduction is when the dislocation can be replaced so that you grasp the patient's hand with both of your hands; and extend their arm, placing your hands around the neck above and below, and push the joint back into place at the wrist or root of the palm until it returns to its proper position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is on the front, it can be reduced by doubling the hand onto itself and pressing the root of the palm against the dislocated neck.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply strong traction; and this is done by two ministers extending the arm, and holding it tight with two cloths so that it does not move during traction. Then twist the arm on both sides, having wrapped a long and wide cloth around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the physician has joined the joint with their hand, they should oil it with some oil to lubricate the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns to its place.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in place, apply a dry compress with egg albumen and press it firmly. Then wrap the arm around the patient's neck and leave it on for a few days before removing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly fixed in its place, remove the bandage and leave it alone. But if you see that the joint is not yet stable, then begin again with the compress and bandaging, leaving it on for a few more days until it is securely fixed, before removing it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if the patient feels pain after reduction of the dislocation and it moves again, then bathe it and rub it gently, pressing firmly until the pain subsides. Or you can apply a poultice of fresh sheep's wool, leaving it on for one day and one night before removing it and immersing the limb in hot water.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when it sweats, rub the joint temperately and then reapply the poultice and immerse it in hot water. Repeat this process two or three times until it is healed. And if necessary, apply a moist cloth heated with butter and press it on the joint for support.
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is easy to reduce, easier than other joints. However, it should be reduced as soon as possible after it occurs, before swelling sets in or inflammation comes.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And reduction is done by placing the affected hand on a table and extending the ministers' hands. The physician then places their palm over the appearance of the dislocation and pushes until it returns to its place.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, you must ensure that the reduction is complete by having the patient place the back of their hand on a table and then extending and reducing it again.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, the patient should place their hand palm down on the table and the physician should place their hand over the appearance of the dislocation. If it returns now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, apply cold compresses to calm inflammation and leave them on without starting again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if the patient cannot tolerate it and you cannot reduce it after a few days, the joint will remain dislocated;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	"And harm nothing to the patient but as long as the hand is weakened, and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves or arteries are cut; so there is no other remedy but to squeeze with a fire cautery near the case, and perhaps nothing else will help."
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	"And when the hand is in its place, put on the dressing that we have said, then bind it and leave it for five days, then untie it and let it remain thus."
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then make him warm water compresses, and rub him until he is free."
de la dislocation des dois de la main	"on the dislocation of the fingers of the hand"
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	"No fingers of the hand are dislocated on any side, none at the back of the palm or belly."
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	"Then grasp the finger, and press on the joint until it returns, then hold the head of the finger and push it towards the part where it is dislocated;"
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	"and leave it for two days, and then put it in a bandage that day; and do not tie it too tightly, as we have said, and untie it the next day, and make him move it, and bind it again loosely; and do this often until it is healed."
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	"And do likewise if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, and do as you have done here until it is healed; and do likewise if it is dislocated elsewhere."
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	"on the dislocation of the shoulder blade of the back"
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the sciatica of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are many dislocations, there is no treatment, for the patient hastens his death.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that evacuations occur without volition, and cannot be held back, and many times some limb is softened, such as both thighs or both arms or one
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And often the sciatica moves in four parts; that which moves at the back is called "gibbosity":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The treatment for gibbosity, if it has come from childhood, is that there should be no hope of recovery or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And those that come from falls, blows, or similar causes, the ancients prescribed various treatments with great words, but they had little benefit in all cases.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have formed diverse instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in gibbosity which comes to the chest before, there is no remedy nor healing
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and likewise that which comes directly into both sides, and one cannot cure it except for that which comes properly onto the back, as I say
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and that the patient should lie on his face on one level surface, and have a blanket under him so he does not hurt himself
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then drive one stake into the ground firmly at the head of the bed, and another at the feet, and tie a rope around the waist of the patient, and another at the hips, knees, and ankles
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and two ministers hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and let them be tied firmly, with the stake as we have said, and the doctor put his palms on the spine forcefully until it returns to its proper place
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a board three feet long and place it under the patient's back while they are on their side, then insert the end of the board under the patient's spine, then place the middle of the board onto the spine
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and let the doctor put his feet on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its proper place; and if you see that it does not work, then do it on the other side which turns towards the hand
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you drive two stakes into the ground at the head of the patient's bed and two others towards their feet, with a space of one palm between each stake, both above and below
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and each stake should have a hole where the rope can be inserted, and they should be firmly in the ground so that they do not move, and between each pair of stakes there should be one turning stake upon which the rope turns, with two small stakes of one palm length on either side to turn the turning stake
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the rope that is between the shoulders to the turning stake towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other turning stake, and each minister turn their stake with all the rope, and the master put the spine back into place as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is aligned, then put on a dried plaster with egg white, then the poultice, and then the iron plate three fingers long that covers the area of the gibosity and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it on with a rope as we have said, and let the patient rest until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	And if any other problems arise at the end of the healing process, then one should administer softening and soothing medications along with the iron plate that we mentioned earlier, and sometimes one may also administer a piece of lead
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and sometimes the appearance of a displaced spine in the lower back may arise, and one might think that it is a dislocation; but it is only the bone which has appeared, so one should not make assumptions about this: for it could lead to death
des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and shoulder only suffer dislocations, unlike other joints, and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back, with more dislocations on the inside than elsewhere, and few dislocations in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the sign of an inner hip dislocation is that when the diseased leg is placed next to the healthy one, it appears longer and the diseased knee joint opens wider than the healthy one, and the diseased leg cannot bend at the knee.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and the location of this dislocations is indicated by the presence of a hot swelling or abscess near the hip joint
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one that comes on the outside is that it is opposite to those that have come before
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of one that happens in front is that he walks well with his leg completed; nonetheless, he cannot bend his knee without pain, and if he wants to walk forward, he cannot do so, and he retains his urine, and the angle swells, and when he walks, he walks on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of one that happens behind is that he cannot straighten or bend his knee, and his leg is twisted compared to the other one, and the angle is softened, and the hip joint is located beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this type of hip dislocation is that you should ascertain whether the dislocation is recent or old, and if it has remained in its position for some time, then there is no need for treatment; but one must not make assumptions about this.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case of a fresh hip dislocation, which can occur in four ways, you should quickly put the joint back into place, and stretch it inside and outside, and move it to the right or left; perhaps it will return to its proper position, and no other treatment is necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return to its proper position in this way, then you should prepare one strong assistant and stretch the leg strongly with both hands or use a rope tied above the kneejoint
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another assistant places their hands under the shoulders and then ties a soft rope around the hip, while another holds onto the end of the rope
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and all pull upwards and downwards at once so that the patient is lifted off the ground and remains suspended
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching applies to all four types of hip dislocation, and if the dislocation has returned to its proper position as we have said, then that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	But if not, then you must treat it according to its type. If the dislocation is on the inside of the hip joint, then you should have the patient lie on their healthy side, put a rope around the root of the thigh and below the angle, then pull the rope up towards the angle and the groin
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then another assistant should take the patient's arms and embrace the large area of the diseased thigh and stretch it outwards forcefully: now it will return to its proper position, and this type of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot reduce it using the method I have described, then you should tie both of the patient's feet together with a soft rope around both ankles and both knees, and stretch the diseased leg two spans further than the other one
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then he should be hung from the head of a beam, and let him hang two arm-lengths above the ground; then command one minister to embrace the top of the thigh, and let another minister hang with the patient embracing the thigh tightly, for the joints return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	"And when the dislocation is at the thigh, let the patient lie down as we said for one with dropsy, and stretch one leg properly upon the sick limb, and also upon the foot."
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	"Then place two pieces of wood: one at the head and one at the feet, then insert one piece of wood between the thighs of the patient in this shape:"
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	"And place moist bandages around to prevent scorching the patient, then each assistant extend towards him, and let the physician put his hand evenly on the dislocation."
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	"If it returns to its place, that is good. If not, place two boards on top of it and press down as we said in the case of dropsy, then let the patient lie on their healthy side."
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	"And when the dislocation is anterior, it is necessary to extend the sick limb quickly, and according to what I have said; then let the physician place his knee upon the angle of the sick leg, then press with his other hand and stretch downward towards the knee."
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	"And if the dislocation is posterior, it is not necessary to extend the patient downward or lift them up from the ground, but rather they should be positioned as if their hip had been dislocated backwards, just like we said about childbirth on two hips."
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	"and they should be lying on their face, and the bandage stretched out as we said earlier, and one must press upon the joint with the board."
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	"And it will be known that the patient has recovered when they extend their legs and they are even. Then adjust the thighs, place the splint, and fasten with a bandage so that the hip does not move."
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	"And let him rest for three or four days, then remove the splint and place it back on. If you see that they are even, then fasten again as before and leave it for another three days. Then remove it and let him go gently until the member is comfortable."
de la dislocation dou genoil	"Of dislocation of the knee"
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	"The kneecap can be dislocated in three ways: inward, outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward."
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	"And the sign is that you tell the patient to bend their leg towards their thigh, and if it does not articulate with their thigh, know that it is dislocated."
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	"And the reduction of all these types is that you make the patient sit up straight and extend their leg if they can. Then place your back against their face and put your foot on theirs."
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	"Then take their kneecap in your palms and draw it between your thighs, then bend both sides of the knee forcefully. Another assistant should extend the patient's foot until the kneecap returns to its place, and the sign is that it articulates easily with the thigh."
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	"And place the splint on it and keep the leg articulated with the thigh for three or four days, then remove it. The patient should not walk until the member is comfortable."
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the limb is not well placed, one must extend it forcefully as we said in the treatment of the hip until it is healed."
de la dislocation dou talon	"Of dislocation of the heel"
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	"The heel can sometimes be dislocated and sometimes completely dislocated, both inward and outward."
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	"And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it points forward towards the part where it is dislocated:"
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	"The reduction is easy, and one must extend it gently with both hands when it is only sprained."
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	"And when it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit up straight and have one assistant pull them forward by the leg above the ankle;"
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	"then pull the foot towards your right hand and then your left hand twice, then extend it upwards and gently put the foot back in place;"
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	"and do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good. If not, start again, for it may return;"
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	"and if it cannot be reduced in this way, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground and firmly stick a peg in the earth between their thighs. Then tie the straps around so that they do not hurt the patient;"
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	"then have one assistant hold the thigh and another extend the foot with both hands or with one hand holding it at the ankle;"
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	"then each assistant should extend equally, and the peg should always be between the patient's thighs to hold them down when extending;"
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	"then the surgeon must gently push the dislocation back into place with both hands while another assistant holds the healthy leg below. The dislocation will return quickly."
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	"And when it is in place, put on the splint and bandages and strap the foot to the leg tightly. Be careful of the nerves that are behind the ankle joint so that the straps are not too tight;"
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	"then leave it for two or three days and if the straps have loosened, tighten them. Then remove them on the fourth or fifth day, but do not let the patient walk for four days;"
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	"and if they walk before this time, there is no certainty that it will not dislocate again."
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if inflammation occurs afterwards, you must calm it as we have said elsewhere until it is healed."
des dois	"of the fingers"
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	"When the fingers are dislocated, they should be gently extended without force, and this is an easy matter."
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	"And if the dislocation is at any knuckle of the hand, you should make the patient sit on a low stool or table with their back straight. Then place your foot on what opens from these joints and press down hard until it returns;"
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"and when it is equal and nothing opens, place a two-legged table under the sole of the foot. Then extend it forcefully and leave it for three days before removing it. Let them rest until they are healed."
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	"of wound and dislocation together"
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wishes to reset it,
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	"If you are not presumptuous in the treatment, if you are wise in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and if you are compassionate, merciful, and careful, not hasty."
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	"And at the beginning of the treatment, use soothing remedies for hot inflammation, and leave the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of recovery."
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	"And when you see hope, then set the limb back in place before the hot inflammation comes."
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	"Once the limb is back in place, apply remedies to cool the inflammation and treat the wound with drying ointments as needed."
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	"And if there is also fracture along with the dislocation, and small bones are dislocated, set them and do what we have said for simple fractures."
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	"And guard yourself from taking the path of fear, as I have said, for it is better for you to die according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body. Amen."
Explicit le romen de fisique	"The book of physics ends"
